Purpose : Sodium fluorescein ( ‘fluorescein’ ) is the most commonly used diagnostic ophthalmic dye for clinical assessment of the ocular surface . An increase in fluorescein staining presents after the use of certain multi - purpose solutions ( MPS ) and contact lenses , which is a clinical phenomenon known as solution induced corneal staining ( SICS ) . The clinical relevance and mechanisms underpinning fluorescein staining however is conflicting in the literature . Currently a number of studies indicate fluorescein localises within cells that are healthy and metabolically active , in contrast to conventional thought that fluorescein staining of MPS treated cells is indicative of cellular toxicity ; however the precise mechanism underpinning fluorescein internalisation is unknown . The aim of this doctoral thesis was thus to investigate novel biological mechanisms mediating fluorescein uptake and to determine the chemical inducers of increased fluorescein staining . Methods : Spectrofluorimetry was used to analyse the fluorescence intensity of various fluorescein solutions and of tear samples after fluorescein application to the ocular surface . For assessment of fluorescein uptake in cell cultures exposed to test MPS , fluorescence microscopy was performed ; subsequently a high content analysis ( HCA ) microscopy methodology developed in this thesis , was used to enumerate fluorescein fluorescence intensity . The physiological state of cell cultures treated with a number of MPS and fluorescein were also assessed using propidium iodide ( PI ) , Caspase - 3 antibody for apoptosis analysis , metabolic activity assays and confocal microscopy . Endocytosis , macropinocytosis , and receptor - mediated uptake , mechanisms which previous to this work have not been investigated in association with SICS and fluorescein uptake , were studied using chemical inhibitors and serum starvation in cell culture , and then analysed by HCA . To study the hyperfluorescence inducing properties of MPS components , surfactant Tetronic 1107 ( an MPS surfactant component typically overlooked and not investigated as an inducer of SICS ) and Triton X - 100 ( a surfactant not found in MPS ) were exposed to cell cultures and after fluorescein treatment , were analysed by HCA ; metabolic activity assessment of identically treated cultures were also performed . Similarly , HCA and metabolic activity measurements were also performed in cell cultures treated with MPS biocides PHMB and Polyquaternium - 1 ( PQ - 1 ) . Results : Fluorescein fluorescence intensity was not affected by temperature , by alkali solvents , or by different MPS formulations ; concentration remains the primary factor by which fluorescein intensity is affected . It was seen that after 1 % w / v fluorescein instillation on the ocular surface , fluorescein concentration in tear samples significantly decreased within the first minute and decreased to as little as 0 . 0001 % w / v after 10 minutes . Fluorescence microscopy and HCA techniques revealed that on treatment with Biotrue® ( Bausch + Lomb , referred to as P - PQ1 - 1107 ) and ReNu Sensitive Multi - purpose Solution® ( Bausch + Lomb , referred to as P - 1107 ) , fluorescein uptake increased in cell cultures , as typically seen clinically . Also typically seen clinically , cell cultures treated with Opti - free Replenish® ( Alcon ; PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 ) and Complete Revitalens® ( AMO ; PQ1 - Alex - 904 ) did not induce hyperfluorescence . Significantly , only those cells treated with PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 and PQ1 - Alex - 904 exhibited an increase in PI and loss of metabolic activity . Additionally , given that no significant Caspase - 3 staining in all test MPS cells was seen by fluorescence microscopy and blebbing was only observed by confocal microscopy in P - PQ1 - 1107 treated cells , increased fluorescein hyperfluorescence is unlikely to be related to apoptosis . Study of various biological internalisation mechanisms revealed that dynamin ( a protein associated with endocytosis ) inhibition in P - PQ1 - 1107 or P - 1107 treated cells significantly decreases fluorescein uptake with no detrimental effect to cell metabolic activity . Interestingly , on quantifying fluorescein uptake in surfactant treated cells , a significant increase in hyperfluorescence was measured with only Tetronic 1107 at concentration 1 % w / v with no significant effect on cellular metabolic activity . In contrast , cell culture treatment with biocides PHMB , and PQ - 1 did not induce increased fluorescein uptake comparable to MPS P - PQ1 - 1107 or P - 1107 ; metabolic activity assays revealed that this is likely attributed to the decrease in cell metabolic activity exhibited with these biocides . Conclusions : The differential fluorescein staining associated clinically with four varied MPS was also seen in an unique in vitro model , allowing the subsequent study of the SICS phenomenon and the fundamental basis of fluorescein uptake . Using this in vitro model , it was seen that fluorescein internalisation is associated with the protein dynamin in healthy , metabolically active cells , and is unlikely to be mediated by apoptosis . Moreover , fluorescein uptake is induced by surfactant Tetronic 1107 and not biocides PHMB or PQ - 1 , which is in contrast to the popular belief that increased hyperfluorescence is induced by the biocide component of MPS . 18 Declaration No portion of the work referred to in the thesis has been submitted in support of an application for another degree or qualification of this or any other university or other institute of learning . This is for you . 22 Chapter 1 Introduction and Background 23 1 . 1 . Background to thesis The fluorescent topical dye sodium fluorescein ( often referred to as fluorescein only ) is used to assess the integrity and health of the ocular surface . Once fluorescein is instilled on the eye , corneal and conjunctival staining ( or ‘hyperfluorescence’ ) is observed using a slit - lamp biomicroscope . The occurrence of fluorescein hyperfluorescence is typically associated with poor ocular health . In association with certain multi - purpose solutions ( MPS ) and contact lenses , ocular hyperfluorescence increases : a phenomenon known as solution induced corneal staining ( SICS ) . Although there are a number of hypotheses proposed for the mechanism underpinning such increased hyperfluorescence , it is in fact poorly understood . Given that fluorescein is the primary ophthalmic diagnostic dye used clinically , it is vital to fully understand the mechanisms underpinning fluorescein hyperfluorescence so as to improve clinical understanding of fluorescein staining and to better understand the relevance of SICS . There are three overall aims to this work , the first being to investigate how the ocular surface affects the intensity of fluorescein fluorescence . The second was to study the biological mechanisms underpinning fluorescein uptake in cell culture , and finally to identify chemical inducers of increased hyperfluorescence . The specific aims were : 1 . To identify potential physiochemical characteristics that may affect fluorescein fluorescence staining on the ocular surface . 2 . To develop an in vitro model of SICS that with exposure to MPS exhibits the same differential fluorescein fluorescence responses as demonstrated by these MPS clinically . 3 . To develop a method by which SICS can be quantified as a means to analyse the effect of MPS on fluorescein uptake in cells . 4 . To further study the association between hyperfluorescence and cellular health . 24 5 . To elucidate a specific uptake mechanism underpinning fluorescein staining . 6 . To identify , if any , a single MPS component responsible for increased hyperfluorescence . 1 . 2 . Thesis overview This thesis is organised into seven chapters . Chapters three through to six are formatted using the alternative journal thesis format in preparation for future publication : each of these chapters includes an abstract , introduction , methods , results and discussion section . A summary of each chapter is described below : Chapter 1 – Introduction to thesis aims and review of the current literature . Chapters 2 - This section details the standard and already established protocols regularly used throughout the thesis . Chapter 3 – This chapter describes the various methods explored for fluorescein quantification in cell culture , and explains the principal choice to use high content analysis ( HCA ) . Chapter 4 – Fluorescein at various concentrations and temperatures , interaction with varied pH and MPS were investigated as possible contributors to the fluorescence intensity of fluorescein observed on the ocular surface . These are evaluated using spectrofluorimetry and a novel method developed for the quantification of fluorescein concentration on the ocular surface . Chapter 5 - Murine fibroblasts ( L929 cells ) and human corneal cells ( HC cells ) are used to study the variable effects of different MPS on fluorescein uptake , and explore its effects on cellular health using necrosis , apoptosis and metabolic activity assays . Dynamin - dependent uptake is explored as a method of cellular fluorescein internalisation . Furthermore , non - ionic surfactants Tetronic 1107 and Triton X - 100 are investigated in both cell lines as hyperfluorescence inducers . 25 Chapter 6 – Change in mitochondrial oxidative phosphorylation , receptor mediated uptake and macropinocytosis are investigated as further mechanisms underpinning fluorescein uptake . The effect of biocides PHMB and Polyquaternium - 1 on cellular metabolic activity and fluorescein uptake are also studied . Chapter 7 - This chapter summarises the overall findings and limitations of this thesis , and discusses future work required in this field . 26 1 . 3 . The cornea and its function The cornea is a transparent dome - like structure on top of the iris , lens and anterior chamber , and accounts for approximately two - thirds of the eye refractive power ( Jacob 2016 ) . The cornea receives its nutrients from tear , aqueous and the perilimbal vasculature , and its oxygen from the atmosphere by tear film , and also by perilimbal capillaries . The layers of the cornea are organised into epithelium , Bowman’s membrane , stroma , Dua’s layer , Descemet membrane , and endothelium ( Jacob 2016 ) ; these layers can be seen in Figure 1 . Figure 1 : Layers of cornea structure : ( a ) Epithelium ( b ) Bowman’s Membreane ( c ) Stroma ( d ) Dua’s layer ( e ) Descemet’s membrane ( f ) Endothelium . Image taken from Mastering Endothelial Keratoplasty ( Jacob 2016 ) . Epithelium 1 . 3 . 1 . The corneal epithelium , along with the tear film , is integral in maintaining a smooth refractive surface , and provides a mechanical barrier to pathogens . It is made up of non - keratinised , stratified , squamous epithelial cells , five to seven layers thick . The outermost layer consists of two to three layers of fully differentiated superficial cells tasked with maintaining tear film stability by secreting glycocalyx . Loss of glycocalyx causes a loss of tear stability , and a breakdown of the ocular optical system ( Delmonte & T . K . Kim 2011 ) . The surface area of superficial cells varies with type of measurement used , where using specular microscopy the mean area has been measured as 628 . 2 ± 13 . 4 µm 2 ( Tsubota et al . 27 1996 ) whereas by confocal microscopy , mean area was measured as 913 ± 326 µm 2 ( Mustonen et al . 1998 ) . The corneal epithelium however changes proportionally to continuous wearing time of extended wear soft contact lenses ( Tsubota et al . 1996 ) . The layer underneath the superficial layer is comprised of wing cells , two to three layers thick , named so due to its morphology . These are less flat than the superficial cell layer , and are in an intermediate state of differentiation . Basal cells , a single layer of columnar epithelium 20µm tall , located beneath the layer of wing cells , are the only cells that have the mitotic ability to differentiate into wing and superficial cells ( Jacob 2016 ; Delmonte & T . K . Kim 2011 ) . The epithelium layers can be seen in Figure 2 . Figure 2 : Illustration of the layers of the corneal epithelium . ( A ) Superficial cells ( B ) Wing cells ( D ) Basal cell . Image taken from Figure taken from Mastering Endothelial Keratoplasty ( Jacob 2016 ) . Epithelial cell turnover 1 . 3 . 2 . It is suggested that equilibrium between mitosis , cellular migration and shedding of epithelial cells is integral in epithelial regeneration . The corneal epithelium regenerates every 7 to 14 days , where daughter cells differentiate into wing cells and migrate to the surface ( Jacob 2016 ) . Bowman’s membrane 1 . 3 . 3 . The Bowman’s membrane is an acellular structure measuring 10µm thick , which lies between the basal corneal epithelium and the anterior stroma . It is composed of predominately collagen types I and III , which are continuous with the anterior stroma and 28 helps maintain the shape of the cornea . It also acts as a barrier to trauma . However , it does not possess the ability to regenerate and it will form a fibrous scar on injury ( Jacob 2016 ) Stroma 1 . 3 . 4 . The stroma constitutes 90 % of the total corneal thickness , and is predominately composed of collagen fibrils types I , III , V and VI ( Jacob 2016 ) . The stroma contains approximately 200 - 250 bundles of collagen fibres , called lamellae ( Delmonte & T . K . Kim 2011 ) . Transparency and biomechanical strength of the stroma relies on the precise organisation of lamellae , and are arranged using uniform and regular spacing ( Jacob 2016 ) . Scattered within the lamellae there are highly metabolically active cells called keratocytes . These cells are integral to maintaining the extracellular matrix environment ( also required for stromal transparency ) ( Delmonte & T . K . Kim 2011 ) by synthesising collagen and proteoglycans of the stroma ( Jacob 2016 ) . Keratocytes also contain a soluble protein called “crystallins” that further contribute to maintaining corneal transparency ( Delmonte & T . K . Kim 2011 ; Jester et al . 1999 ) . Dua’s layer 1 . 3 . 5 . This layer is a tough , well - defined acellular lining between the stroma and the Descemet’s membrane measuring 10 . 15±3 . 6µm thick ( Dua et al . 2013 ) . It is composed of thicker fibrils than those in the stroma , and are composed in 5 – 8 lamellae of predominantly type I collagen that run in longitudinal , transverse , and oblique directions ( Jacob 2016 ; Dua et al . 2013 ) . Its recent discovery will potentially influence corneal surgery where it has been suggested that it can be used to generate tissue for endothelial transplant in the instance of deep anterior lamellar keratoplasty ( DALK ) ( Dua et al . 2013 ) . Descemet’s membrane 1 . 3 . 6 . This is a separate layer between the Dua’s layer and the endothelium , and measures approximately 8 - 10µm thick . It primarily comprises of collagen types III and VIII contributing to the elasticity of this layer along with glycoproteins fibronecton , laminin and 29 thrombospondin . This membrane has been deposited by endothelial cells derived from the neural crest ( Tuft & Coster 1990 ; Jacob 2016 ) . The endothelium 1 . 3 . 7 . The corneal endothelium is a monolayer of hexagonal cells ( sometimes described as a “honey - comb like mosaic” ; ( Delmonte & T . K . Kim 2011 ) ) that lines the posterior corneal surface , and is approximately 10µm thick at birth . The cells flatten in adulthood , and thickness reduces to 4µm . Human endothelial cells are arrested in the G1 phase of the cell cycle with no mitotic activity , although the reason for this is unknown . Nevertheless , the endothelium barrier is permeable enough to mediate the osmotic gradient required for the deturgesced state of the stroma . Change in endothelial cell morphology can detrimentally contribute to endothelial cell ability to deturgesce the cornea ( Delmonte & T . K . Kim 2011 ) . 1 . 4 . Ocular dyes Within ocular healthcare Rose Bengal , Lissamine Green B and sodium fluorescein ( fluorescein ; abbreviated to FL throughout thesis ) are three commonly used dye used to detect ocular lesions or diseases . Lissamine Green B is a synthetic organic acid made up of two amino phenyl groups ( Norn , 1973 ) . Rose Bengal is a chemical derivative of fluorescein ( Romanchuk 1982 ) , where fluorescein itself is a xanthene product of resorcinol and pthalic anhydride first demonstrated by von Baeyer in 1871 . Chemical structures of FL , Rose Bengal and Lissamine Green B are shown in Figure 3 . 30 Figure 3 : Molecular structures of Sodium fluorescein ( left ) , Rose Bengal ( centre ) and Lissamine Green B ( right ) ( J . Kim 2000 ) . Rose Bengal 1 . 4 . 1 . Kim describes that the use of Rose Bengal did not become popular within the ophthalmic community until 1933 when a common Rose Bengal staining pattern in keratoconjunctivitis patients was recognised ( J . Kim 2000 ) . Several studies show that Rose Bengal does not stain healthy cells , but dead or degenerated cells ( Norn 1967 ; Norn 1969 ; Norn 1970 ) . Interestingly , the interaction of Rose Bengal and tear proteins have shown certain proteins could bind to and subsequently block Rose Bengal uptake in cell culture , however it is unlikely that the same extent of protein - Rose Bengal binding would occur on the ocular surface ( Tseng & Zhang 1995 ) . Rose Bengal has been used to study dry eye ( as reviewed in Doughty 2013b ) , but has also been used to characterise unstable tear film ( Lee & Tseng 1997 ) , and as an aid in locating cells for impression cytology ( Doughty 2013a ) . Lissamine Green B 1 . 4 . 2 . The Lissamine Green B ( Lissamine Green ) clinical staining profile is similar to that of Rose Bengal demonstrated by ( Norn 1973 ) although it should be noted that Rose Bengal induces more irritation of the ocular surface compared to Lissamine Green ( Khurana et al . 1991 ; Machado et al . 2009 ) . Lissamine Green has been shown to similarly stain dry eye patients comparable to Rose Bengal ( Machado et al . 2009 ) , utilised to stain the bulbar conjunctiva ( Manning et al . 1995 ) and marginal conjunctiva ( Doughty et al . 2004 ) . 31 Both Lissamine Green and Rose Bengal are available as sterile strips impregnated with 1 . 5mg of the compound . However , given Rose Bengal has shown to cause more discomfort more often than any other vital dye , Lissamine Green is the preferred dye to study ocular health ( J . Kim 2000 ; Korb et al . 2008 ) . In fact , the Association of British Dispensing Opticians ( ABDO ) , reports that due to the “discomfort and stinging on insertion " , Lissamine Green has replaced Rose Bengal as the preferred conjunctival stain and Rose Bengal is no longer available in the UK ( McNamee 2012 ) . Sodium fluorescein 1 . 4 . 3 . The molecular formula of fluorescein is C 20 H 10 O 3 Na 2 , with a molecular weight of 376 . 27 g / mol . It is a disodium salt and is available as a red / orange crystalline powder ; nevertheless , at 15°C it has 50 % solubility in water ( Romanchuk 1982 ) . As later discussed , there are many ophthalmic uses for fluorescein but it is not limited to the area . It is applied to a plethora of diverse disciplines such as oceanography to tract currents in and marine biology to determine skin damage in fish ( Hart et al . 2003 ; Livengood et al . 2013 ; Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . 1 . 5 . Fluorescence profile of Fluorescein Fluorescein is a fluorescent molecule . A fluorescent compound has its own excitation and absorption spectra causing each dye to emit fluorescence at a specific wavelength . FL can be excited at 480 - 500nm which then fluoresces green between 500 - 600nm ( Noga & Udomkusonsri 2002 ) . The maximum excitation and emission wavelengths however are reported as 490nm and 530nm ( Romanchuk 1982 ) . Molecular basis of fluorescence emission 1 . 5 . 1 . When fluorescent molecules are exposed to certain wavelength of light , the absorbed light causes fluorphores to enter a higher singlet electronic state ( S 1 or S 2 ) from its ground state ( S 0 ) . As fluorophores return to S 0 , a photon is emitted , which is detected at a longer but 32 lower energy wavelength than its excitation wavelength ; this is observed as fluorescence . Fluorescence is typically illustrated by a Jablonski diagram as shown in Figure 4 . Figure 4 : Jablonski diagram adapted from Principles of Fluorescence Spectroscopy ( Lakowicz 2013 ) . 1 . 6 . Factors affecting fluorescein fluorescence on the ocular surface Clinically , fluorescein is available as single sterile use solution vials of 1 % or 2 % Minims ( Chauvin Pharmaceutical Ltd by Bausch + Lomb ) or as 1mg sodium fluorescein Fluorets . Upon administering fluorescein to the eye , there are several factors that need to be considered such as concentration , pH , length of exposure and number of applications . Fluorescein concentration 1 . 6 . 1 . Maximum fluorescence can be achieved at 0 . 001 % w / v concentration of fluorescein , although there are discrepancies in the literature regarding the specific concentration ( Romanchuk 1982 ; Nichols et al . 2012 ) . Fluorescein concentration however demonstrates a non - linear relationship with fluorescence , which is typically taken into consideration in clinical practice ( Romanchuk 1982 ; Ossewaarde - Van Norel et al . 2002 ; Shotton & Habeeb 1955 ; Tan et al . 2013 ) . Fluorescein nevertheless exhibits self - or concentration quenching , where quenching occurs above concentrations that induce the maximum fluorescence ( Romanchuk 1982 ) . The process of quenching is a reversible loss of fluorescence , and is a Internal S 0 S 1 S 2 Fluorescence Absorption Absorption 33 unique property of fluorescent compounds ( Lichtman & Conchello 2005 ) . There are several possible mechanisms by which quenching can occur such as Fluorescence Resonance Energy Transfer ( FRET ) , or contact quenching ; these mechanisms of quenching have been used in the development of oligonucleotides and peptides probes , and of molecular beacons to target specific nucleic acids and peptides ( Marras et al . 2002 ; Johansson & Cook 2003 ; Crisalli & Kool 2011 ; Marras 2006 ) . Other mechanisms of quenching include collisional quenching ( Eftink & Ghiron 1976 ) , and charge transfer quenching ( Föll et al . 1990 ) . Fluorescein in high concentrations will appear yellow whilst in more dilute concentrations it will appear green . This is because at higher concentrations , the maximum emission spectrum is shifted towards a longer wavelength ( Romanchuk 1982 ) . Fluorescein fluorescence intensity can also be reduced by simple absorbance - based quenching , demonstrated by Rose Bengal as the quencher in a study by Doughty ( Doughty 2014 ) . There is little information in the literature regarding the concentration of fluorescein on the ocular surface . Peterson and colleagues have tested four different fluorescein instillation methods : 1 % Minim , 2 % Minim , a single drop of saline on a fluoret , and fluoret moistened with saline with the excess shaken off ( Peterson et al . 2006 ) . Quenching was observed with all fluorescein instillation methods , however levels of “useful fluorescence” were achieved by 1 % minim and the moistened fluoret quicker than 2 % minim and the fluoret moistened with a single drop of saline only . Although it was identified that fluorescein application with 1 % Minim achieved the greatest intensity , the specific concentration of fluorescein available on the ocular surface at the time of viewing was not quantified ( Peterson et al . 2006 ) . However in a different study by Glasgow , after 22mM fluorescein application and fluorescein intensity measurement in corneal cells removed by cytology , fluorescein was seen to quench from 1 to 16 minutes after instillation of fluorescein . This was observed despite fluorescein concentration having decreased below the quenching threshold in the 34 tear film ( Glasgow 2016 ) . Further study of fluorescein concentration on the ocular surface is required to understand the physiochemical properties of fluorescein at the time of clinical observation . pH 1 . 6 . 2 . Fluorescein absorption and emissions spectra are affected by the pH of its environment ( Romanchuk 1982 ) . At an acidic pH , fluorescein will fluoresce a blue / green whereas at an alkali pH , it will fluoresce yellow ( Romanchuk 1982 ) . It has been reported that fluorescence intensity increases with pH of solution where on reaching pH 8 , it will start to decrease , whilst others reported this at pH 6 ( Shotton & Habeeb 1955 ) . Between pH 7 and 8 , an effect on its absorption or emission spectra is not detected ( Romanchuk 1982 ) . On the ocular surface , fluorescein is subjected to the ocular surface tear fluid . The average pH on the ocular surface tear fluids in normals vary across studies ( pH 6 . 93 ± 0 . 24 as reported by ( Norn 1988 ) , and pH 7 . 83 ± 0 . 1 as reported by ( Chen & Maurice 1990 ) , and also over the course of the day ( Coles & Jaros 1984 ) ) . However , it does not exhibit the acidic or slightly alkali conditions that have been reported to cause significant changed in fluorescein absorption or emission spectra . Length of exposure to Fluorescein 1 . 6 . 3 . Due to its quenching properties , fluorescein fluorescence intensity is likely dependent on the time of observation of the ocular surface after application . However , the duration of time the ocular surface is exposed to fluorescein also has an effect on the intensity seen . The study by Hickey and colleagues investigated this aspect by exposing the eyes of rabbits to 100µl of 2 % fluorescein for various lengths of time : 15 seconds , 30 seconds , 1 minute and 4 minutes ( Hickey et al . 1973 ) . On causing injury to the cornea , maximum fluorescein intensity had been reached after 15 seconds of fluorescein exposure . Moreover , on measuring intensity after 48 hours , by which point full recovery from injury had been achieved , fluorescence was lost only for those stained for 15 seconds . This suggests that 15 35 seconds of exposure is a sufficient length of time to detect injury as well as minimise staining of healthy corneal epithelium . Number and layering of fluorescein application 1 . 6 . 4 . The intensity of fluorescence seen on the ocular surface is also affected by the number of times fluorescein is applied ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . The process of sequential fluorescein instillations has been investigated in six subjects who exhibited staining in preliminary experiments ( stainers ) and one control subject who exhibited no staining in preliminary experiments ( non - stainers ) ( Josephson & Caffery 1992 ) . A solution of 2 % fluorescein was sequentially applied 7 times over a 28 - minute period in all seven subjects , and examined by one examiner using a cobalt blue filter and number 12 Wratten yellow enhancement filter . This process was repeated every 2 hours over a total of 12 hours . All stainers exhibited staining at all time - points , with increased incidence of staining observed at the first of the instillations ( at 0800am ) , although the amount and area of staining differed . Some subjects who did show sequential staining , also underwent overnight patching of the eye , which did not influence the incidence of staining in these corneas ( Josephson & Caffery 1992 ) . However , the mechanism for this increase in corneal staining is not understood ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . Furthermore , the ‘thickness’ of the dye also causes variation in staining seen . In this sense , the term ‘thickness’ refers to the amount of dye that layers on top of the eye . This factor is affected by the composition and quantity of tear fluid ( Eliason & Maurice 1990 ) . Morgan and colleagues give an example of this where exaggerated blinking can rectify the initial lack of fluorescence in a patient as this causes the dye to dissipate and overcome the quenching effect ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . The most common ophthalmic uses of fluorescein are discussed below . 36 1 . 7 . Ophthalmic application of Fluorescein Pfluger in 1882 demonstrated breaks in corneal epithelium by use of sodium fluorescein , and this saw its introduction into the ophthalmic community ( J . Kim 2000 ) . Now , due to its spectral and synthetic chemistry properties , it is one of the most utilised fluorescent dyes in scientific research ( Lavis et al . 2007 ) . TBUT 1 . 7 . 1 . Fluorescein is frequently used to confirm symptomatic dry eye by analysis of the tear break up time ( TBUT ) . It is used as a measurement of tear stability but is not a reflection of aqueous quantity in tears ( Murube 2003 ) . The classic method of assessing TBUT is to apply sodium fluorescein into the eye and to analyse the break up pattern using a slit - lamp ( Pult & Riede - Pult 2012 ) . The Schirmer’s test ( ST ) designed by Otto Schirmer in 1903 is another method of diagnosing dry eye , which further allows the quantification of lacrimal secretion ( Murube 2003 ) . Although ST does have poor sensitivity in detecting dry eye condition , this can be overcome by analysis of fluorescein meniscus time ( FMT ) instead . FMT is a measurement of the rate of tear meniscus formation ( Kallarackal et al . 2002 ) . It was concluded that FMT is a more sensitive method for assessing tear production in comparison to ST ( Kallarackal et al . 2002 ) . It is interesting to note that TBUT , nonetheless , is the most sensitive method in detecting the stability of lacriminal tears ( Kallarackal et al . 2002 ) . Retinal and iris angiography 1 . 7 . 2 . In addition , fluorescein is used in iris angiography as a means of exposing ocular pathologies such as glaucoma , retinal vascular occlusions and tumour , a few examples amongst many ( Brancato et al . 1997 ) . This also indirectly but confidently allows analysis of retinal circulation ( Brancato et al . 1997 ; Rechtman et al . 2009 ) . Retinal ( fundus ) angiography is also a major use of fluorescein , which is used to assess vascular flow of the retinal vessels in diabetes ( Sakata et al . 2007 ) and in some forms of age - related maculopathy ( Rosenfeld et al . 2006 ; Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . 37 Epithelial permeability 1 . 7 . 3 . Moreover , as a research tool , fluorescein is used to assess epithelial permeability that may occur as a result of soft contact lens wear ( McNamara et al . 1998 ) and use of toxic drugs and preservatives ( Joshi et al . 1996 ) . It is found that any subsequent trauma is highlighted by the uptake of fluorescein that occurs as a consequence of an increase in cell permeability ( Joshi et al . 1996 ) . As such , epithelial barrier function is relative to permeability of the corneal epithelium to fluorescein ( P dc ) ( McNamara et al . 1998 ) . 1 . 8 . Corneal staining with Fluorescein Practice dictates fluorescein is most commonly used as a stain to assess corneal integrity ( K . W . Ward 2008 ) . The term ‘staining’ refers to the hyperfluorescence observed on application of fluorescein and subsequent illumination with cobalt blue light ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . Ocular staining is commonly associated with corneal epithelial defects ( Maldonado - Codina et al . 2013 ; Tabery 1992 ) , such as with ocular disease ( Jie et al . 2008 ; McMonnies 2007 ) , following trauma ( for example alkali burns or corneal abrasions ) ( Wipperman & Dorsch 2013 ; Fante & Trobe 2014 ; S . A . Wilson & Last 2004 ; Smally et al . 1992 ; Scarlett & Gee 2007 ) and with certain MPS and contact lens wear combinations ( Andrasko & Ryen 2008 ; Carnt , Willcox , et al . 2007 ) . Corneal staining observed in non - contact lens wearers is typically referred to as ‘background staining’ : of 102 non - contact lens wearers examined , 79 % of corneas exhibited some form of staining when using the CCLRU photographic grading scale ( discussed in more detail in Section 1 . 8 . 1 ) in a study by Dundas and colleagues ( Dundas et al . 2001 ) . In another study , it was similarly seen that the median staining grade of 16 non - contact lens wearers was 0 . 5 using a 0 to 4 grading scale ( Schwallie et al . 1997 ) . Observation of fluorescein of the ocular surface is typically performed using a standard white - bulb slit - lamp biomicroscope . A blue filter is used to minimise the wavelength of spectral radiation from the white bulb to better match fluorescein excitation wavelengths , 38 and an additional barrier filter ( yellow ) is used to optimise viewing fluorescein fluorescence at 510 - 520nm . An example of ocular surface staining with and without a yellow filter can be seen in Figure 5 ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . Figure 5 : Corneal surface observed using a slit lamp biomicroscope without ( A ) and with ( B ) a yellow barrier filter ; adapted from Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 . Grading systems 1 . 8 . 1 . Corneal surface fluorescence ( CSF ) is classified according to several parameters that include shape , intensity and location of fluorescence ; a summary of which can be found in Table 1 . A B 39 Table 1 : Classification of CSF with key descriptors ; adapted from Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 . Grading systems have been developed for CSF to classify its severity specifically for contact lens wearers ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . Staining can be assigned according to the Efron scale , which consists of single values : the increase from 0 to 4 represents an increase in severity ( Efron 1998 ) . This can be seen in Table 2 . Table 2 : Efron grading scale , adapted from Efron 1998 . The type , extent and depth of staining can also be scored according to the Cornea and Contact Lens Research Unit ( CCLRU ) grading system . Again , each variable is assigned a grade from 0 to 4 depending on severity ( Table 3 ) . This scale has been used to determine staining amongst healthy individuals so as to differentiate from pathological corneal Mucin balls Dimple veil SICS Foreign body Smile Superior epithelial 3 & 9 Intensity Coalescent Coalescent Punctate or diffuse Coalescent Calescent or diffuse Coalescent Punctate or diffuse Shape Circular Circular Annular or circular Linear Arcuate or band Arcuate Patch Location Any corneal area Commonly central or mid - peripheral All corneal areas , sometimes with central sparing Any corneal area Inferior Superior Nasal and / or diffuse Grade Definition Interpretation 0 Normal No tissue changes 1 Trace Clinical action not required 2 Mild Clinical action may be required 3 Moderate Clinical action usually required 4 Severe Clinical action urgently required 40 staining ( Dundas et al . 2001 ) . Solution induced corneal staining ( SICS ) The term ‘stain’ or ‘staining’ refers to the ocular surface fluorescence seen , and again this is commonly associated with corneal epithelial defects ( Maldonado - Codina et al . 2013 ; Tabery 1992 ) . SICS however is described as a discrete , superficial punctate staining of the corneal epithelium ( L . W . Jones & D . A . Jones 2001 ) . One of the first cases of solution induced corneal staining ( SICS ) demonstrated was in 2002 by Jones and his team . They found superficial punctate staining with the use of polyaminopropyl / polyhexamethylene biguanide ( PHMB ) preserved solution ReNu Multiplus® ( Bausch + Lomb ) in Pure Vision ( balafilcon A ) contact lenses ( Bausch + Lomb ) ( L . Jones et al . 2002 ) . Staining can take on an annular pattern where it concentrates in the peripheral cornea , or it can spread evenly across the cornea ( Fonn 2010 ) . Such staining is readily observed on application of soft contact lenses that have been stored in certain MPS ( Bandamwar et al . 2010 ; Garofalo et al . 2005 ) . A number of clinical studies have been performed to document the effects of Grade Type Extent Depth 0 Absent Absent Absent 1 Micropunctate 1 - 15 % surface involvement Superficial epithelial involvement 2 Macropunctate 16 - 30 % surface involvement Stromal glow present within 30seconds 3 Coalescent macropunctate 31 - 45 % surface involvement Immediate localised stromal glow 4 Coalescent patch 1mm or greater in size 46 % or greater surface Immediate diffuse stromal glow 41 various contact lens solutions and contact lens materials on fluorescein fluorescence as discussed below . Since 2002 , many studies have been conducted exhibiting the SICS phenomenon ( Garofalo et al . 2005 ; Bandamwar et al . 2010 ; Andrasko & Ryen 2008 ) . Some of these studies were extensive such as the IER Matrix Study ( Carnt , Willcox , et al . 2007 ) and the Andrasko Staining Grid ( Andrasko & Ryen 2008 ) . Corneal Staining Grid 1 . 9 . 1 . Andrasko and colleagues have documented the effects of SICS in the presence of various MPS and contact lens material combinations ( Andrasko & Ryen 2008 ) in the Andrasko Staining Grid ( accessible at www . staininggrid . com ) . This staining grid is regularly updated , and as of July 2017 the most recent staining grid can be seen in Figure 6 . Contact lenses were pre - soaked in the test MPS overnight and were then inserted into subjects for 2 hours of wear . For corneal staining assessment , sodium fluorescein ( 0 . 6mg FUL - GLO ophthalmic strip ) was instilled into each eye and examined using a cobalt filter and a yellow Wratten number 12 filter . Corneal staining was then graded in 5 corneal regions : central , superior , inferior , nasal and temporal . This was then averaged to assign a staining area percentage to each eye . To determine an overall average staining area percentage for each MPS and lens combination , the eye with the maximum staining area for each subject was then averaged with the worst eye of all other subjects . The Andrasko Corneal Staining Grid is uniquely colour coded , where each colour represents the severity of staining observed . For instance , green represents insignificant staining of less than 10 % of the cornea , yellow represents 10 - 20 % staining and staining of above 20 % is represented as the colour red . Widespread staining suggests a change in contact lens care should be considered . As seen in Figure 6 , PHMB - based MPS such as Biotrue® , ReNu Fresh® and ReNu Sensitive Multi - purpose solution® cause the most 42 staining in both Hydrogel and Silicone - Hydrogel contact lenses . For example , staining was observed in as large as 73 % of the corneal surface with MPS ReNu Fresh® and Purevision Hydrogels . In contrast , Polyquad / Aldox solutions ( for example Opti - Free Replenish® and Opti - Free Express® ) cause insignificant staining in all contact lens materials tested , where the maximum area of staining of 7 % was observed . However , it must be acknowledged that the data represents only 2 hours of lens wear , and the results of this study may not be indicative of long - term MPS / lens wear . Figure 6 : The Andrasko Corneal Staining Grid accessed 11 July 2017 ( www . staininggrid . com ) . Dillehay and colleagues however question the statistical and clinical relevance of the methodology and data analysis used in the work by Andrasko ( Dillehay et al . 2007 ) .
