The Institute for Eye Research ( IER ) matrix study 1 . 9 . 2 . The IER matrix study , conducted in 2007 , followed groups of 40 subjects for 3 months of lens wear . Each group was tested a combination of MPS and silicone hydrogel lens , where 16 different combinations were tested . Corneal staining was then graded from 0 to 4 in the central , superior , inferior , nasal and temporal zones of the cornea at baseline , two weeks , one month and finally at three months : 0 signifies no staining , 1 = ≤ 5 % , 2 = 6 to 10 % , 3 = 16 - 30 % and 4 = > 30 % . The results of this work are shown in Figure 8 . Each percentage is representative of patients who exhibited SICS per month . 44 Direct comparisons between the Andrasko Corneal Staining Grid and The IER Matrix study cannot be made as the area of staining in the Andrasko Corneal Staining grid is assessed after only 2 hours of lens wear . Nevertheless , long - term use of Opti - Free Express® and Opti - Free Replenish® was seen to cause a greater SICS response in combination with Acuvue® Oasys™ , O 2 Optix™ , and PureVision® lenses , in contrast to short - term wear of 2 hours . That is , the combination of Polyquad / Aldox based MPS was seen to induce more corneal staining with a larger range of silicone hydrogel lenses than PHMB - based AQuify® MPS . Figure 8 : IER Matrix Study data ; percent of patients per month ( taken from Carnt et al . 2007 ) . 1 . 10 . Multi purpose solutions ( MPS ) composition Different MPS will cause varying levels of staining , suggesting that the various components of MPS may be responsible for this . Components of MPS include preservatives , buffers , surfactants and chelating or wetting agents ( Sorbara et al . 2009 ) . Future work , however , could benefit from a thorough analysis of different combinations of MPS components and their effect on staining . 45 Preservatives 1 . 10 . 1 . To avoid adverse effects ( Alfonso et al . 2006 ; Joslin et al . 2007 ) , MPS contain preservatives such as polyquaternium - 1 ( PQ - 1 ) , polyaminopropyl / polyhexamethylene biguanide ( PHMB ) ( Sorbara et al . 2009 ) or benzalkonium chloride ( BAK ) ( Richardson et al . 1977 ) . Not only do preservatives provide antimicrobial activity in the bottle , but they also deter decomposition of active compounds in solution ( Noecker 2001 ) . The afore - mentioned preservative based MPS are more commonly used over hydrogen peroxide ( H 2 O 2 ) based solutions due to convenience and low costs ( Woods et al . 2007 ) . H 2 O 2 is not any less an effective antimicrobial agent when compared to PQ - 1 or PHMB , and as it is utilised in lieu of lens - solution incompatibilities , it still plays an important role in lens care ( Papas et al . 2007 ) . There are two methods of neutralising H 2 O 2 giving rise to one - step and two - step systems . The one - step neutralisation system is achieved by either catalytic platinum , or by the release of catalase in form of a tablet , both of which can be located within the contact lens storage case ( Hiti et al . 2005 ) . Two - step systems require soaking in a second catalytic solution 10 minutes prior to lens wear . Each system has been tested for its antimicrobial activity , and it was found that a one - step system undergoes neutralisation too rapidly and as such , a two - step system for storage and disinfection ( against Acanthamoeba specifically ) has been recommended ( Hiti et al . 2005 ) . Biguanides have been recognised as potent antimicrobial agents from as early as 1946 by Curd and Rose , and as such has given rise to polymeric hexamythelene biguanides such as PHMB . It has been found that as polymer length increases , so does its microbial activity ( Broxton et al . 1983 ) . PHMB binds to the bacterial envelope and displaces the otherwise stabilizing Ca 2 + , which leads to a loss of transport , biosynthetic and catabolic capability ( Gilbert & Moore 2005 ) . Also possessing antimicrobial activity is Polyquaternium - 1 . It is a 46 quaternary ammonium compound that causes perturbation of bacterial cytoplasmic membrane and of the outer - membrane in Gram - negative bacteria ( Gilbert & Moore 2005 ; Codling et al . 2003 ) . It has been reported that by simply excluding the preservative component in MPS , or switching to use of a MPS with a different preservative , can alleviate symptoms of SICS ( L . W . Jones & D . A . Jones 2001 ) . This suggests that it could play an integral role in explaining the mechanism of SICS . Surface - active agents ( Surfactants ) 1 . 10 . 2 . Cleansing the lens before disinfection is highly recommended by practitioners ( Christie & Meyler 1997 ) . For use in hydrogel lenses , there are two main types of cleaners . Enzymatic cleaners cause breakdown and subsequent removal of proteins , where surfactant ( daily ) cleaners remove and cleanse lenses of lipids and mucus ( Christie & Meyler 1997 ) . Surfactants are also traditionally used as wetting agents with the expectation that they are adsorbed on the lens and are subsequently increasing the wettability of the lens surface ( Lin & Svitova 2010 ) . Surfactant molecules , which possess polar and non - polar components , form micelles in aqueous solutions at concentrations above what is called the critical micelle concentration ( CMC ) ( Cui et al . 2008 ) . Micelles typically from spherical complexes with a dry non - polar hydrophobic core and a polar hydrophilic exterior ( Long et al . 2015 ) . Despite lens care systems being divided into surfactant cleaners , single - purpose disinfecting solutions or multi - purpose solutions , it was seen that all solutions that contain surface - active ingredients are the most effective in protein / spoliation removal ( Franklin 1997 ) . The efficacy of cleaning ability of a lens care solution however does vary with surfactant . Typical examples of surfactants are poloxamers such as Pluronic® , and poloxamines such as Tetronic® , both of which are block copolymers constituted by 47 poly ( ethylene oxide ) and poly ( propylene oxide ) ( PEO and PPO respectively ) . Block co - polymers typically exhibit increased ability to form micelle - like structures in comparison to common surfactants ( Sandez - Macho et al . 2015 ) . Examples of these surfactants can be seen in Figure 9 and Figure 10 where in contrast to Tetronics® , Pluronics® are linear in shape . The effect of the cleaning capabilities of MPS containing Pluronic® and Tetronic® surfactants investigated in an in vitro model was seen to increase with surfactant molecular weight : Tetronic® 1304 > 904 , and Pluronic® 127 > 87 ( Franklin et al . 2013 ) . Figure 9 : Structure of poloxamer Pluronic® F127 ( Ivanova et al . 2000 ) Figure 10 : Structure of poloxamine Tetronic® 1107 ( Flor et al . 2010 ) Chelating agents 1 . 10 . 3 . The most commonly used chelating agent in MPS is ethylene diamine tetra - acetic acid ( EDTA ) . EDTA is a chelating agent that sequesters metals such as calcium to act synergistically with the preservatives in MPS , enhancing antimicrobial activity of lens care solutions ( Christie & Meyler 1997 ; Bartlett 2013 ) . 1 . 11 . SICS and toxicity The word ‘toxic’ is used rather liberally to describe the corneal staining fluorescence associated with MPS and is sometimes used in spite of a lack of damage to the cornea . Even though the data regarding the aetiology behind SICS is inconclusive and requires 48 clarifying , there are some studies that have been able to identify products that are responsible for SICS using scanning electron microscopy ( SEM ) ( Tchao et al . 2002 ) . Begley et al . ( 1994a ) investigated possible toxicity of two different MPS , a PHMB - based solution ( ReNu® Multi - purpose solution ) and a one - step a H 2 O 2 system ( AOsept® ) , in 85 hydrogel contact lens wearers ( Begley et al . 1994a ) . It was found that generally ReNu® caused more staining that AOsept® . Nevertheless , as staining was not severe enough to stop contact lens wear , Begley et al . were hesitant to assign any significance of the staining found to successful hydrogen lens wear . Furthermore , testing on rabbit corneas was undertaken with lenses soaked in either a polyquaternium - based solution ( Optifree Express® ) , ReNu® Multi - purpose solution ( PHMB - based ) , AOsept® or saline as a control . Again , ReNu® Multi - purpose solution showed the most effect on the corneal tissue and this was identified by use of SEM ( Begley et al . 1994b ) . Nevertheless , there is much ambiguity surrounding the issue . For example , the studies discussed are demonstrating the elevated toxicity of PHMB based solution in comparison to others . However , in vitro studies show polyquaternium - 1 based solutions are more cytotoxic ( McCanna et al . 2008 ; Wright & Mowrey - McKee 2005 ) . As stated by Lim et al . ( 2009 ) , caution should be used when predicting clinical responses from data gathered in vitro ( Lim et al . 2009 ) . Care should also be taken when comparing data from various studies . They highlight that even if the same MPS are tested across the studies of interest , cytotoxicity measurements will vary if different cell lines and tests / assays / methods are used ( Lim et al . 2009 ) . One study has shown that SICS that can typically be seen with fluorescein , Rose Bengal and Lissamine Green , can also be visualised without ( Maldonado - Codina et al . 2013 ) . The punctate staining seen is reported to be the same size as an individual epithelial cell . This 49 suggests that the localised areas of fluorescence are in fact individual cells ( Maldonado - Codina et al . 2013 ) . The particular phenomenon of SICS needs to be investigated much more thoroughly , extending the studies to include the several other components that are also present in MPS . 1 . 12 . Mechanisms of cellular fluorescence Surface pooling 1 . 12 . 1 . Surface pooling occurs where fluorescein accumulates within depressions of the corneal epithelium ; the formation of ‘mucin balls’ is an example of this ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ; Pritchard et al . 2000 ; Millar et al . 2003 ) . Little is known regarding the composition of these spherical bodies but they are currently described as a unique form of tear debris ( Pritchard et al . 2000 ) . They are typically 50µm in size and as they reside between the back surface of a hydrogel contact lens and the corneal epithelium , they are immobilized here ( Millar et al . 2003 ) . On removal of the contact lens and subsequent application of fluorescein , the dye is said to pool within the depression caused by the mucin balls ( Szczotka - Flynn et al . 2011 ) . It has also been suggested that the mechanism of surface pooling can be attributed to the ‘dimple veil’ effect that occurs in rigid lens wearers ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . The trapping of air bubbles cause indentations on the corneal surface and causes pooling of the dye ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ; Szczotka - Flynn et al . 2011 ) . However , surface pooling does not account for the punctate staining found in non - contact lens wearers as stated by Jones and Jones ( L . W . Jones & D . A . Jones 2001 ) . Furthermore , excessive blinking or irrigation does not remove the punctate stain and therefore surface pooling over irregularities such as indentations is unlikely ( Mokhtarzadeh et al . 2011 ; G . Wilson et al . 1995 ; Bandamwar et al . 2012 ) . 50 Uptake by dead cells 1 . 12 . 2 . Conventionally , fluorescein was thought to enter a cell when membrane integrity was comprised through lysis . Thus , this theory dictated that only damaged cells would be stained . However , in contrast to these previous beliefs , fluorescein does in fact stain healthy cells in addition to damaged cells ( J . Kim 2000 ; Hickey et al . 1973 ) . It has been suggested that staining of a seemingly healthy cell may not be indicative of an adverse reaction , but may actually be a part of normal cell growth . This is suggested because cells undergo desquamation , and through mitotic or apoptotic processes are regenerated ( Brautaset et al . 2008 ) . Further explanations include the movement of fluorescein from a damaged cell to healthy cells through transmembrane tight junctions ( Romanchuk 1982 ) . Loss of cell junction integrity 1 . 12 . 3 . Tight junctions form a continuous intercellular barrier between epithelial cells and separate tissue spaces , and so selectively regulate the movement of solutes across the epithelium ( J . M . Anderson & Van Itallie 2009 ) . The tight junctions themselves are made up of a protein complex of transmembrane and cytoplasmic proteins ( Hartsock & Nelson 2008 ) , and this forms a high resistance barrier ( Cavet et al . 2012 ) . Impact of MPS on this barrier function can be determined by analysing the expression of the tight junction proteins mentioned ( Cavet et al . 2012 ) . Damage to , or loss of , cell junction integrity is thought to enable fluorescein to permeate the corneal epithelium ( Feenstra & Tseng 1992 ) . This phenomenon is also known as the ingress model . 1 . 13 . New theories of fluorescein staining Active transport as a mechanism of fluorescein staining 1 . 13 . 1 . In presence of MPS ReNu Multiplus® , recent research suggests that fluorescein staining is seen in metabolically active , viable cells only ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) . Fluorescence microscopy and high content analysis showed fluorescein stained cells rarely also stained with propidium iodide , a necrosis marker . This phenomenon was observed in murine 51 fibroblasts , epithelial ( Vero ) and telomerase - immortalised human corneal epithelial ( hTCEpi ) cells . This in support of further findings that fluorescein staining is actually an active process . That is , fluorescein uptake into cells required active and viable cells . Active transport , by definition , is an ATP requiring process . ATP is mainly generated from glucose catabolised using three pathways : glycolysis , tricarboxylic acid ( TCA or Krebbs ) cycle , and oxidative phosphorylation with the latter process generating large amounts of ATP by ATP synthase ( Bonora et al . 2012 ) . Briefly , murine fibroblasts were incubated with ReNu Multiplus® and fluorescein at 37°C , and were subsequently washed and observed at 4°C ( a temperature where active transport is suppressed ) , to show no change in the proportion of hyperfluorescent cells for up to 100 minutes . This was however in contrast to cells washed and observed at 37°C , where a significant decline in hyperfluorescence was seen . Similarly , temperature was also seen to affect fluorescein entry into cells where only 3 . 1±0 . 8 % of MPS - treated exhibited hyperfluorescence when treated with fluorescein at 4°C compared to 54 . 9±7 . 0 % at 37°C ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) . These findings are additionally in support of a number of studies that show fluorescein localises within the cells using confocal microscopy ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ; Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) , and impression cytology ( Mokhtarzadeh et al . 2011 ) . Preservative associated transient hyperfluorescence ( PATH ) hypothesis 1 . 13 . 2 . Preservative associated transient hyperfluorescence ( PATH ) is a radically alternative hypothesis proposed for SICS , and is said to provide an explanation for the MPS related transient corneal hyperfluorescence observed ( Bright et al . 2012 ) . A liposome - based model of the corneal epithelial surface was used to investigate the interaction of preservatives ( PHMB and PQ - 1 ) , fluorescein and cellular membrane components . It was shown that free fluorescein molecules ( FL 2 - ) did not associate with liposomes in contrast to fluorescein - tagged PHMB and PQ - 1 . Significantly , free fluorescein associated with liposomes in the presence of PHMB . Clinically , it is thus suggested that PHMB associates to the human 52 corneal epithelial surface anionic / zwitterionic sites , which then mediates a temporary association of FL 2 - molecules . It is this association of fluorescein to the corneal epithelium that is then observed as hyperfluorescence . It was additionally suggested that PQ - 1 may also mediate fluorescein to the corneal epithelium surface , however due to the disruption caused to membrane integrity by PQ - 1 and the weak association of FL 2 - to PQ - 1 , fluorescence signal may not be clinically visible ( Bright et al . 2012 ) . Hyperfluorescence in apoptotic cells 1 . 13 . 3 . Recent research also indicates hyperfluorescent cells may be apoptotic ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) . Apoptosis is also known as programmed cell death , which allows the organism to control cell number and tissue size ( Hengartner 2000 ) . Live , dead and apoptotic corneal epithelial cells were identified after treatment with various stress stimuli ( preservative , hypertonicity , hypotonicity , scratch and alkaline wounding ) and fluorescein ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) . A greater level of fluorescein fluorescence was seen in apoptotic cells across all treatments , including control ( PBS ) treated cells whereas necrotic cells exhibited low levels of fluorescence . This work suggests clinical hyperfluorescence is representative of apoptotic but still viable cells , and that fluorescein can be used as a probe for apoptotic epithelial cells . This work was conducted using Hoechst 33342 , PI and Annexin - V to stain for individual cells , necrotic cells and apoptotic cells respectively . Briefly , Annexin V is a marker for phosphatidylserine ( PS ) ; PS is translocated from the inner plasma membrane to the cell surface early - on in the execution phase of apoptosis ( Boersma et al , 2005 ) . The localisation and presence of the fluorescence of stained cells observed by fluorescence microscopy was then used to identify the physiological status of each cell . However , as the Annexin - V used was conjugated to a red fluorophore , this may have interfered with any red fluorescence exhibited by PI , causing difficulties in measuring genuine apoptosis ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) . 53 In this thesis however , the association between hyperfluorescence and apoptosis was investigated using the downstream protease of the apoptosis pathway : cleaved ( thus activated ) Caspase - 3 . Caspase - 3 , also known as an executioner or effector caspase , exists as a procaspase dimer when inactive , which prevents accidental activation of the apoptosis pathway . Executioner caspases ( such as caspase - 3 , - 6 , and - 7 ) are activated when the large and small subunits of the procaspase dimer are cleaved , bringing the active sites together to produce a functional protease . This activation is performed by initiator caspases , ( such as caspase - 2 , - 8 , - 9 and - 10 in mammals ) and are activated by dimerization induced by upstream signalling events . Once a single executioner caspase has been activated , it can go on to cleave and activate further executioner caspases , forming a feedback loop for the apoptosis pathway ( Riedl & Shi 2004 ; J . Li & Yuan 2008 ; McIlwain et al . 2013 ) . 1 . 14 . Mechanisms of extracellular uptake In this thesis , active uptake of fluorescein was investigated . Phagocytosis , endocytosis and macropinocytosis are a few of the mechanisms that mediate the uptake of extracellular material into the cell . Phagocytosis is specifically the uptake of large particles , typically > 0 . 5µm . In Metazoa , phagocytosis is primarily utilised by specialised phagocytic cells such as macrophages and neutrophils , for the uptake and degradation of infectious components contributing to the immune response . In lower organisms , phagocytosis is used to acquire nutrients ( Martinet et al . 2009 ) . Endocytosis however is the uptake of proteins , lipids , extracellular ligands and soluble molecules in endocytic vesicles . Endocytosis can be categorised into clathrin - dependent , caveolin - dependent and clathrin / caveolin - independent mechanisms ( Doherty & McMahon 2009 ) . The various mechanisms and pathways of endocytosis are shown in Figure 11 . Endocytosis and macropinocytosis are discussed in further detail below . 54 Figure 11 : Mechanisms of endocytosis ( Mayor & Pagano 2007 ) Clathrin - dependent endocytosis 1 . 14 . 1 . Clathrin - mediated endocytosis is the uptake of materials using lattice - like clathrin coated vesicles , and is utilised by all known eukaryotic cells . The clathrin protein , once recruited to the sites of vesicle budding and after vesicle formation , is recycled back into the cytoplasm for reuse in the next cycle of clathrin - mediated uptake . This form of endocytosis regulates surface expression of proteins , samples the cell’s environment for growth and guidance cues , brings nutrients into cells , controls the activation of signalling pathways , retrieves proteins deposited after vesicle fusion , and turns over membrane components by sending components for degradation in lysosomes ( McMahon & Boucrot 2011 ) . For inhibition of clathrin - mediated endocytosis , targeting specific interaction domains of nucleation and clathrin - pit formation are advised . Potassium depletion , monodansylcadaverine ( MDC ) , phenylarside oxide ( PAO ) , cytosolic acidification , hypertonic shock using sucrose , and chlorpromazine have also been used as clathrin - mediated endocytosis inhibitor , yet with pleiotropic effects ( McMahon & Boucrot 2011 ) . 55 Dynamin , a multi - domain protein containing a GTP - ase module , is essential to clathrin - mediated endocytosis ( Kirchhausen et al . 2008 ; Macia et al . 2006 ) and interacts with several actin - binding proteins ( Jeng & Welch 2001 ; Orth et al . 2002 ; Kessels et al . 2001 ) . Although the precise mechanism of dynamin is still unclear , a number of studies indicate that it is a mechanochemical enzyme , assembling at the neck of a budding vesicle resulting in membrane fission and vesicle formation ( Preta et al . 2015 ; Kirchhausen et al . 2008 ; Macia et al . 2006 ) . Dynasore is utilised as a reversible inhibitor of dynamin ( Tsai et al . 2009 ; Hernaez & Alonso 2010 ; Barrias et al . 2010 ) , and was used throughout the work in Chapter 5 . This “small interfering molecule” was identified by Macia and colleagues in 2006 whom propose that dynasore inhibits clathrin - mediated endocytosis by acting on two discrete steps : the transition from half formed ( “U” ) pit to fully formed ( “O ) pit , and the subsequent fully formed pit to endocytic vesicle ( Macia et al . 2006 ) . However , as dynamin has also been identified in a number of other pathways ( McMahon & Boucrot 2011 ; Hinshaw 2000 ) , it indicates that dynamin inhibition using dynasore is not specific to clathrin - mediated endocytosis only ( McMahon & Boucrot 2011 ) . Further to this , dynasore has been shown to effect cellular processes involving cholesterol , lipid rafts and actin ( Preta et al . 2015 ) , with the latter more generally associated with several types of endocytosis ( Jeng & Welch 2001 ) . Caveolin dependent endocytosis 1 . 14 . 2 . Endocytic pathways independent of the clathrin protein , such as caveolin dependent endocytosis , was discovered when inhibition of clathrin - dependent endocytosis did not affect the uptake of a number of other types of cargo . There are three types of mammalian caveolin proteins : caveolin - 1 and - 2 are found primarily in non - muscle cells ( with the exception of neurons and leukocytes ) in contrast to caveolin - 3 , which is muscle specific ( Doherty & McMahon 2009 ) . Chemical inhibitors of caveolin dependent ( and lipid - raft dependent - endocytosis ) typically target cholesterol ; for example , inhibition of cholesterol 56 biosynthesis by statins , extraction of cholesterol from the plasma membrane using cyclodextrins , use of filipin and nystatin to sequester cholesterol within the plasma membrane and modification of cholesterol with cholesterol oxidase ( Smart & R . Anderson 2002 ; Ivanov 2008 ) . Clathrin - and Caveolin - independent pathways 1 . 14 . 3 . Extracellular fluid , SV40 virions ( Damm et al . 2005 ) as well as receptors for a number of molecules ( Kirkham & Parton 2005 ) have been shown to be internalised by endocytic events independent of clathrin - and caveolin - 1 endocytosis ( Doherty & McMahon 2009 ) . Additionally , GPI - linked proteins typically undergo endocytosis via a cholesterol - dependent but clathrin - independent pathway ; these associated endosomes are known as GPI - AP - enriched early endosomal compartments ( GEECs ) ( Sabharanjak et al . 2002 ) . In Chinese Hamster Ovary ( CHO ) cells , stably transfected FR α is taken up by the GEEC pathway , which has been shown to be downstream of clathrin - independent carriers ( CLICs ) ( Sabharanjak et al . 2002 ) . This is referred to as a CLIC / GEEC pathway ( Doherty & McMahon 2009 ) and was shown to be tubular ( or “ring shaped” ) in morphology when viewed by EM in Mouse Embryonic Fibroblasts ( MEFs ) ( Kirkham & Parton 2005 ) . On disruption of the CLIC / GEEC pathway , internalisation of GPI - linked proteins occurs via clathrin - mediated endocytosis instead ( Sabharanjak et al . 2002 ) , although it is unclear whether cargo is delivered to the correct destinations ( Doherty & McMahon 2009 ) . Inhibition of CLIC / GEEC effector proteins such as Cdc42 , Arf1 and GRAF1 , will significantly reduce uptake of cargo ( Nonnenmacher & Webber 2011 ) . Macropinocytosis 1 . 14 . 4 . Bulk and non - specific uptake of extracellular liquid is otherwise known as macropinocytosis , while the mechanisms of uptake described above can be defined as pinocytic ( Doherty & McMahon 2009 ) . First observed in 1931 , macropinocytosis is the earliest understood mechanism of the eukaryotic endocytic pathways ( Kerr & Teasdale 2009 ) . The activation of receptor tyrosine kinases causes a global rise in actin - 57 polymerisation at the cell surface . Rho GTP - ases and phosphoinositide 4 , 5 - bisphosphate initiate actin - polymerisation by activating WASp / Scar proteins . The assembly of Arp2 / 3 complex with an actin monomer onto a pre - existing actin filament are co - ordinated by these proteins . The newly extended actin filament pushes the plasma membrane into a planar membrane ruffle and eventually fuses back with the plasma membrane encapsulating large volumes of fluid while doing so . The mechanism behind the folding back of the ruffles to form macropinosomes is however not fully understood ( Kerr & Teasdale 2009 ) . There are three major inhibitors of macropinocytosis known : agents that target sodium - proton exchange , F - actin polymerisation and phosphoinositide metabolism . These inhibitors can also be used to inhibit phagocytosis ( Ivanov 2008 ) . Throughout the work in Chapter 5 , the sodium - proton exchange inhibitor 5 - ( N - ethyl - N - isopropyl ) amiloride ( EIPA ; a more potent analogue of inhibitor Amiloride ) was used to inhibit membrane ruffling associated with macropinosome formation ( Fretz et al . 2006 ; Kerr & Teasdale 2009 ) . The mechanism by which sodium - proton exchange inhibitors ( such as Amiloride and its analogues ) inhibits macropinocytosis is unknown , but research indicates that macropinocytosis is inhibited by a decrease in cytosolic pH affecting GTPase activation and actin assembly by Amiloride / EIPA action ( Koivusalo et al . 2010 ) . 1 . 15 . Cell culture Developing an in vitro ocular cell based alternative has its benefits in that it can provide species - specific responses , which in turn allows a good basis for clinical predictions ( Kruszewski et al . 1997 ) . Over the last 20 years , corneal cell culture models have been rapidly developed and used to study areas of interest such as corneal response to ophthalmic drugs ( Ranta et al . 2003 ) . In these instances , adherent cells are used , which require an attachment surface . This is typically a tissue culture plastic treated by electric ion discharge for a net negative charge . To further aid cell attachment , surfaces can be 58 treated with a matrix product such as collagen type IV , fibronectin or laminin ( Freshney 2006 ) . In contrast to adherent cells , suspension cell lines do not require treated tissue - culture vessels ; an example of a suspension cell line is lymphocytes ( HL60 cells ) . Models can utilise primary ( cells isolated from donor tissue ) or continuous cell cultures ( cultures that exhibit extended lifespan by chemicals or viruses , also known as transformed or immortalised ) from a range of species . Continuous cell lines typically have a number of advantages over the primary in that the isolation of tissues , subsequent harvesting and purification of cells is not required ( Hornof et al . 2005 ) . Although these cells remain stable for a many passages and can thus provide a large number of cells per experiment in contrast to primary cells , their gene expression profile may significantly change from the native cells ( Tian et al . 2004 ) . Primary cell cultures 1 . 15 . 1 . Primary cultures are difficult to use for in vitro modelling due to their short life span and biological variability ( Toropainen et al . 2001 ) . Studies into obtaining epithelial cells from various parts of the cornea have shown that human ocular limbal epithelium grows better than the peripheral ocular epithelium ( Ebato et al . 1988 ) , whereas the peripheral ocular epithelium grows better than the central corneal epithelium ( Ebato et al . 1987 ) . Human primary corneal cells have been used to study the effect of endogenous basement membrane components ( such as laminin and fibronectin ) on cell attachment ( Ohji et al . 1994 ; Ohji et al . 1993 ) , the proliferative effects of conditioned media and growth factors ( Pancholi et al . 1998 ) and to study toxicity effects of natural tear substitutes ( Geerling et al . 2001 ) . Human corneal epithelial cells ( HCEpiC ) is an example of a primary culture . A disadvantage of such a primary cell line is that these cells will normally only survive a maximum of two passages ( Toropainen et al . 2001 ) . It shows a very low transepithelial 59 electrical resistance ( TEER ) value of 144 Ω / cm 2 , and so even though it forms stratified structures and desmosomal junctions similar to the in vivo situation , its poor epithelial barrier function makes it unsuitable for permeability studies ( Hornof et al . 2005 ) . Transformed cell cultures 1 . 15 . 2 . There are many methods by which primary cells lines may be immortalised . Primary human corneal epithelial cells infected with Adeno 12 - SV40 hybrid virus or transfected with plasmid RSV - T ( Kahn et al . 1993 ) produced HCE - T cells ( transformed human corneal epithelial cell line ) . Dependent on culture conditions , this cell line will grow in a monolayer or in stratified layers . However , abnormal organisation of wing cells in the mid - corneal zone and basal cells can cause problems especially as the significance of such organization is not clear in vivo ( Toropainen et al . 2001 ) . Human corneal epithelial cells immortalised by SV40 infection however exhibits the typical cobblestone - like appearance ( Araki - Sasaki et al . 1995 ) . Primary corneal epithelial cell lines have also been immortalised with transfection of tetracycline - responsive human papilloma virus ( HPV ) 16 - E6 / E7 and exhibit typical corneal cell morphology ( Mohan et al . 2003 ) . Another example of immortalised cell culture are telomerase - immortalised human corneal epithelial cell line ( hTCEpi ) , developed by infection with human telomerase reverse transcriptase ( hTERT ) ( Robertson et al . 2005 ; Gipson et al . 2003 ) . When immortalised with hTERT , the cell line life span increases , exhibits genetic stability and maintains the ability to differentiate ( Morales et al . 2003 ) . Nevertheless , special consideration needs to be observed depending on the application of its use : for instance , although hTERT cells have not shown to induce ( by itself ) cell transformation , it is recommended to proceed with applications such as cell therapy with caution ( Milyavsky et al . 2003 ) . Keratocytes ( fibroblastic cells ) have also been developed to grow continuously as monolayers , and have been seen to form tight barriers between cells ( Niederkorn et al . 60 1990 ; Goskonda et al . 1999 ) . This particular cell culture was however derived from rabbit , and such cells are referred to as SIRC - cells ( Statens Seruminstitut rabbit corneal cells ) . A number of transport and permeability studies have been performed with this cell line ( Dey et al . 2004 ; Talluri et al . 2009 ; Tak et al . 2001 ) . 3 - D corneal models 1 . 15 . 3 . The primary advantage of a 3 - D corneal model is the ability to replicate in vivo environments much more closely than monolayer cultures ( Rönkkö et al . 2016 ) . A number of models have been developed ( Rönkkö et al . 2016 ) , with the first being in 1999 ( Griffith et al . 1999 ) . This very first model of immortalised human corneal cells comprised of the epithelium , stroma and endothelium , which exhibited typical corneal morphology , biochemical marker expression , transparency , ion and fluid transport , and gene expression ( Griffith et al . 1999 ) . However , building such models are technically complex and time - consuming for the limited number of assays they offer ( Rönkkö et al . 2016 ) . Nevertheless , these limitations are being addressed in the form of commercially available 3D models . For example , EpiCorneal™ by MatTek Corporation have developed a tissue model of normal human corneal epithelial cells cultured to form a stratified , squamous epithelium ( https : / / www . mattek . com / products / epicorneal / ; accessed 30 July 2017 ) . More recently , Wang and colleagues have developed a 3 - D corneal tissue model with epithelium , stroma and innervation with the purpose of further understanding the interaction between corneal innervation and corneal tissues ( S . Wang et al . 2017 ) . This particular model however utilises a silk scaffolding system in contrast to the typical collagen based models ( S . Wang et al . 2017 ; Reichl et al . 2004 ; Suuronen et al . 2004 ) . Such silk - based innervated corneal tissue models may be used in addition to animal models for the study of drug development , disease intervention and investigation of corneal physiology ( S . Wang et al . 2017 ) . L929 cell line 1 . 15 . 4 . L929 is a murine fibroblast cell line , where fibroblasts can be found in many types of tissues such as tendon , ligament and skin ( Theerakittayakorn & Bunprasert 2011 ) . L929 61 cells specifically come from fibroblast connective and adipose tissue of a 100 - day old C3H / An male mouse ( ECACC No . 85011425 Mouse C3 ) . Cell lines such as this are useful models as they can consistently provide large volumes of cells for an extensive period of time . L929 cells are routinely used for across many fields of research due to their ability to reproduce and their biological responses ( Thonemann et al . 2002 ) . It is a cell line popular for material biocompatibility testing ( Brétagnol et al . 2008 ; Serrano et al . 2005 ; Zange & Kissel 1997 ) , drug cytotoxicity testing ( Nordin et al . 1991 ; Faria et al . 2009 ) and cell biology studies ( Theerakittayakorn & Bunprasert 2011 ) . The cells can be grown to 80 - 90 % confluency in 2 - 3 days , and this makes them cost efficient and a reproducible cell line . General drawbacks of cell culture models 1 . 15 . 5 . The obvious drawbacks are the ease by which microbial contamination can occur , as well as the accumulation of necrotic cells and depletion of nutrients in the growth medium . Although these are regularly seen in a working tissue culture laboratory , using a sterile technique and robust protocols , their occurrences can be controlled . The main drawback of cell culture models is that they will never replicate perfectly the in vivo interactions of test subjects and the different corneal cell types and layers ( Zhao et al . 2006 ) . 62 1 . 16 . Summary The literature reviewed demonstrates that fluorescein fluorescence as a result of MPS interaction on the corneal surface is poorly understood , with recent studies contradicting the conventional cytotoxicity argument typically used to explain the SICS phenomenon . Staining grid studies such as those conducted by Andrasko et al ( Andrasko & Ryen 2008 ) and Carnt et al ( Carnt , Willcox , et al . 2007 ) report different findings of MPS component accountability towards SICS . It is proposed the that PHMB based MPS induce increased corneal hyperfluorescence ( Andrasko & Ryen 2008 ) , however the study by Carnt et al indicates PQ - 1 based MPS may in fact be responsible ( Carnt , Willcox , et al . 2007 ) . It is also unclear to what extent the physiochemical properties of fluorescein may be effecting the interpretation of fluorescein staining on the ocular surface at the time of observation . In order to improve patient care and to further our understanding of clinical hyperfluorescence , it is vital to understand the chemical basis underpinning MPS - related hyperfluorescence . There are a number of proposed mechanisms of fluorescein hyperfluorescence ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) , however recent research indicates that fluorescein localises within the cytoplasm of individual cells ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ; Bakkar et al . 2014 ; Mokhtarzadeh et al . 2011 ) . The previous work conducted by this laboratory suggests fluorescein hyperfluorescence is an energy requiring process ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) , although the specific mechanism underpinning fluorescein internalisation is unknown . This active transport theory is in contrast to a number of already proposed mechanisms ( for example , the passive mechanism surface pooling and the ingress model as discussed in Section 1 . 12 ) and as such requires further investigation . 63 The overall aims of this work were thus to ( 1 ) explore the physiochemical properties of fluorescein fluorescence , ( 2 ) investigate active transport mechanisms related to fluorescein internalisation and finally ( 3 ) to study the hyperfluorescence inducing capabilities of major MPS components . Chapter 2 Routine methods and protocols 65 2 . 1 . Introduction Described below in detail are the general standard methods and materials used throughout this work . This includes a description of the cell lines used throughout the thesis , the tissue culture methods employed and description of subsequent treatment with MPS , fluorescein and DNA binding dyes . As described , the effect of test treatments was measured by metabolic activity assay or fluorescence microscopy . In some instances fluorescein intensity or cellular uptake were measured by fluorimeter or high content analysis ( HCA ) respectively . Finally , an overview of the statistical analysis applied is described . Chapters 3 through to 6 each contain a separate “Materials and Methods” section describing the specific experimental protocols used . 2 . 2 . Cell lines Murine fibroblast L929 cells ( ECACC No . 85011425 ) were purchased from The European Collection of Authenticated Cell Cultures ( ECACC UK ) . Human corneal ( HC ) cells were grown from corneas donated by the Manchester Eye Bank ( NHS Blood and Transplant , UK ) . Corneas were pre - consented for research in the case of unsuitability for transplantation ( for example , in the case of low endothelial cell count or incomplete medical history ) . Corneas ( male aged 72 and aged 59 ) were received suspended in maintenance medium . 2 . 3 . Cell culture medium and reagents Dulbecco’s Modified Eagle Medium ( DMEM ) with High Glucose ( Gibco , UK ) supplement with Fetal Bovine Serum ( 10 % ) ( Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) and L - Glutamine , 200mM ( 4mM ) ( Gibco , UK ) , further referred to as growth medium , was used for both L929 and human corneal cell ( HC ) lines . To detach L929 cells from plastic surface , 0 . 25 % Trypsin - EDTA ( Life Technologies , UK ) was used , and 0 . 05 % Trypsin - EDTA in Dulbecco’s Phosphate Buffered Saline ( PBS ; ThermoFisher , UK ) was used for HC cell 66 detachment ; PBS was used to wash attached cells . CTS™ Synth - a - Freeze™ ( Gibco , UK ) , a protein - free liquid cryopreservation medium , was used to for cell cryopreservation . 2 . 4 . Tissue Culture Common Practice All cell lines were maintained in humidified incubators at 37°C and 5 % CO 2 . Tissue culture ( TC ) flasks used were 25cm 2 and 75cm 2 ( Corning , Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) , and multi - well plates used included 24 and 96 well white , clear bottom plates ( Corning , Sigma Aldrich , UK ) and 96 well black , clear bottom plates ( Greiner Bio - one , UK ) . L929 cell culture passaging 2 . 4 . 1 . Once L929 cells reached 80 - 90 % confluency , cells were washed with PBS ( 5ml ) . Trypsin EDTA ( 5ml ) was used for 5 minutes to detach the cells from the flask . Detached cells were quenched using growth medium ( 10ml ) . Cells and growth medium were then centrifuged at 700rcf for 5minutes . After centrifugation , the supernatant was disposed of and pellet was suspended in growth medium to be seeded at the desired density . Cells were passaged every 2 days in this way . Corneal cell culture and passaging 2 . 4 . 2 . Corneal cells were grown from human corneal explants following protocol adapted from Khan et al , 1993 ( Kahn et al . 1993 ) , and is described in 2 . 4 . 3 . 1 . Human corneal epithelial cells usually appear to have a cobblestone morphology ( Ryeom et al . 2000 ) . Growth on tissue culture plastic can however induce a flatter morphology , and as such collagen coating is required for a more rounded morphology ( Gospodarowicz et al . 1978 ) . Substrate stiffness is also an important factor in modulating appropriate cellular differentiation ( Cozzolino et al . 2016 ) . This model at first exhibited both an epithelial and fibroblast growth from segmented explants in collagen coated wells . Fibroblast growth dominated and outgrew epithelial cell population , which was likely aided by serum - containing growth medium ( Kahn et al . 1993 ) . These cells are used throughout this thesis , and are further referred to as human corneal ( HC ) cells . 67 Figure 12 : Corneal cells grown from explants . Typical epithelial morphology ( arrow ) and fibroblast morphology ( circle ) was seen after 7 days of growth ( left ) . 14 day after growth , fibroblast morphology outgrew all cells with typical epithelial morphology ( right ) . Collagen coating 2 . 4 . 3 . Collagen from calf skin ( Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) was diluted to 0 . 01 % using dH 2 O and used to coat multi - well plates and TC flasks at room temperature overnight at 100µl / cm 2 . Corneal cell growth from Corneas 2 . 4 . 3 . 1 . Corneas were revived using growth medium in single tissue culture dishes for 7 days , changing the growth medium once . Cornea was then segmented into 8 pieces . 4 segments were placed epithelial side down into a well of a collagen coated 6 well plate . Each segment was allowed to adhere to the surface at room temperature for 20 minutes before pipetting a drop of growth medium to each segment , and incubating at 37°C and 5 % CO 2 for 2 nights . Thereafter , growth medium ( 3ml ) was added to each well and cell growth was evaluated every 2 nights . Once cells proliferated away from each corneal segment , segments were removed . Growth medium was changed in wells every 2 nights until 80 % confluency was reached . Passaging human corneal cells 2 . 4 . 3 . 2 . Human corneal cells were washed with PBS ( 1ml ) before treating with 0 . 05 % Trypsin EDTA ( 1ml ) for 4 minutes at 37°C and 5 % CO 2 . Once cells had detached from the well , 10 % FBS in PBS ( 2ml ) was added to Trypsin EDTA / cell suspension to neutralise . 7 day growth 14 day growth 68 Suspension was centrifuged at 300rcf for 5 minutes . Supernatant was removed , and pellet was re - suspended in growth medium . Cells were seeded using into tissue culture flasks at 1x10 4 cells / cm 2 . Cells reached 80 % confluency by approximately 48 hours , typical of quick corneal fibroblast growth . Freezing cells 2 . 4 . 4 . Cells at 80 % confluency was trypsinised , pelleted and re - suspended in CTS™ Synth - a - Freeze™ at 1x10 6 cells / ml ; 1ml per vial . Vials were moved to - 80°C in a Mr . Frosty freezing container and then transferred to liquid nitrogen storage after 24 hours . Thawing cells 2 . 4 . 5 . A cryovial was removed from liquid nitrogen storage , and transported to tissue culture hood on dry ice . Immediately , it was placed in a 37°C water bath , and defrosted until a small piece of ice remained . Under sterile condition , cells were transferred into a 15ml falcon tube . Drop wise , pre - warmed growth medium was added to the falcon tube of cells and then transferred to T25 flask . After overnight attachment at 37°C and 5 % CO 2 , spent growth medium was removed and replaced with fresh growth medium . 2 . 5 . MPS and fluorescein treatment of cells Cells treated with MPS 2 . 5 . 1 . The MPS used throughout this thesis are Bausch + Lomb ( Kingston upon Thames , UK ) solutions Biotrue® and ReNu Sensitive Multi - purpose solution® ( previously known as ReNu Multipurpose solution ) , Opti - Free RepleniSH® ( Alcon ; Surrey , UK ) and Complete Revitalens® ( AMO ; High Wycombe , UK ) . A summary of MPS components can be seen in Table 4 . These solutions clinically exhibit a range of fluorescein staining as seen in www . stainingrid . com by Andrasko and colleagues ( Andrasko & Ryen 2008 ) , as well as in studies by Jones et al , 2002 and Kilvington et al , 2010 ( L . Jones et al . 2002 ; Kilvington et al . 2010 ) . Solutions were stored according to manufacturers instructions at room 69 temperature and out of direct sunlight , and were replaced after three months of opening . Cells were seeded using growth medium into 24 well plates at 1x10 5 cells / ml ( 1ml per well ) , or into 96 well plates at 2 . 5x10 4 cells / 100µl , and were grown overnight . After overnight incubation , growth medium was removed and cells were then incubated with MPS ( 1ml in 24 well plate , 100µl in 96 well plate ) for 2 hours . Fresh growth medium was added to control cells for the same 2 hours . Table 4 : MPS formulations . MPS are referred to by biocide and surfactant combinations . P , PQ1 , Aldox , and Alex refer to the biocides PHMB , Polyquaternium - 1 , Aldox and Alexidine dihydrochloride respectively . 1107 , 1304 and 904 refer to surfactants Tetronic 1107 , Tetronic 1304 and Tetronic 904 respectively . Fluorescein treatment of cells 2 . 5 . 2 . A 0 . 1 % w / v fluorescein ( Fluorescein Sodium Salt ; Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) solution was first prepared in PBS . This was then diluted using PBS 1 : 10 to make a 0 . 01 % w / v solutions . This was filtered using a 0 . 22 µ m filter . After MPS , and growth medium treatment for 2 hours , solutions were removed and cells were incubated with fluorescein ( 0 . 01 % w / v in PBS unless otherwise stated , 1ml or 100µl dependent on well size ) for 10 minutes .
