Discussion An in vitro model to investigate the biological basis for fluorescein hyperfluorescence on the corneal surface , using both murine fibroblasts and human corneal ( HC ) cells has been developed in this work . This approach made use of the well - characterised clinical effects of different contact lens MPS on fluorescein hyperfluorescence ( known as SICS ) . Several studies previously proposed that fluorescein hyperfluorescence involves the direct uptake of fluorescein into corneal epithelial cells ( Mokhtarzadeh et al . 2011 ; Kuwayama et al . 2002 ; Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) and this mechanism was the focus of this current work . Previously in this laboratory , it was shown that fluorescein uptake into mammalian cells was temperature dependent , and increased after exposure to ReNu Multiplus® MPS , which contains the surfactant Tetronic 1107 ( and twice the concentration of PHMB ) as in P - 1107 ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) . In the present study , the effects of MPS known to increase or decrease hyperfluorescence clinically , and the biological basis for fluorescein uptake were examined . Notably fluorescein quantification was performed in the present study using a high content analysis ( HCA ) platform which measures the level of fluorescence of each cell . Only one other study has attempted to quantify fluorescein levels in cultured cells ( in that case using conventional fluorescence microscopy ) ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) . It was seen that the MPS formulations which are known to increase hyperfluorescence on the ocular surface ( P - PQ1 - 1107 and P - 1107 ) ( L . Jones et al . 2002 ; Andrasko & Ryen 2008 ; Tilia et al . 2012 ) both cause increased fluorescein hyperfluorescence in L929 fibroblasts and HC cells . Conversely PQ1 - Alex - 904 or PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 resulted in little or no fluorescein staining , once again in line with the clinically observed effects of these solutions ( Kilvington et al . 2010 ; Tilia et al . 2012 ) . It is possible that the interaction of a contact lens material itself with the MPS ( and potentially with the corneal epithelium ) may contribute to the hyperfluorescence observed clinically . However this finding that the clinically observed effects of these four MPS on hyperfluorescence can be reproduced in a 153 simple cell culture model without the presence of a lens material , suggests that SICS may primarily reflect the biochemical effects of the MPS . Different contact lens materials may additionally moderate levels of the MPS components able to reach the corneal surface . It was further confirmed quantitatively that non - viable necrotic cells ( following BKC treatment ) are unable to take up fluorescein ( such cells typically all stained with PI ) . This was consistent with previous findings by this laboratory ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) , and with those of Bandamwar and colleagues who reported minimal fluorescein fluorescence in non - viable human corneal limbal epithelial ( HCLE ) cells ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) . Interestingly MPS formulations P - PQ1 - 1107 and P - 1107 , both of which are associated with clinical hyperfluorescence , produced little PI staining and no significant changes in metabolic activity . Conversely , increased PI staining and loss in metabolic activity were found after treatment with the MPS formulations PQ1 - Alex - 904 and PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 , both of which are clinically associated with low levels of fluorescence . These findings suggest strongly that in contrast with the previously held view that fluorescein hyperfluorescence reflects ‘toxicity staining’ , fluorescein staining in fact indicates an absence of cytotoxicity . When a clinician observes ‘staining’ on the ocular surface , it is therefore not indicative of dead cells but rather indicates metabolically fully functional cells . However nonetheless the presence of MPS increases fluorescein staining in these otherwise healthy cells . In the later stages of our study , the processes - presumably stimulated by MPS P - PQ - 1107 and P - 1107 – may be responsible for this hyperfluorescence were examined . Although it was shown that hyperfluorescence did not correlate with necrosis , it was possible that cells taking up fluorescein were undergoing apoptosis . However , notably none of the test MPS formulations resulted in increased staining for Caspase - 3 , which is a 154 vital downstream protease in the apoptosis pathway ( J . Li & Yuan 2008 ; McIlwain et al . 2013 ) . Interestingly , blebbing ( a morphological change of the cell membrane associated with apoptosis ( Mills et al . 1998 ; Ziegler & Groscurth 2004 ) ) was consistently seen in P - PQ1 - 1107 treated cells . However such morphological change was not observed with P - 1107 treatment even though both formulations are known to increase hyperfluorescence in vitro and in vivo . These data further suggest apoptosis is unrelated to hyperfluorescence . These recent findings are in contrast to a study by Bandamwar and colleagues ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) , who investigated the effect of toxic levels of PHMB on fluorescein staining . However the latter study involved staining for the early apoptotic marker Annexin V tagged with a red fluorophore for cells co - stained with the red fluorescent stain PI . The two stains were differentiated based only on cellular location of red fluorescence , and ‘background’ staining with PI may have been difficult to distinguish from Annexin V staining . This laboratory previously found that fluorescein uptake and egress from the cell are active processes , which are inhibited at low temperature ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) . This was investigated this further here by directly inhibiting dynamin - dependent pathways in L929 and HC cells using dynasore , a reversible inhibitor of dynamin . Dynasore treatment caused a decrease in fluorescein uptake for both control and MPS - treated cells . Dynamin is a GTPase protein implicated in a number of energy dependent endocytic pathways ( Doherty & McMahon 2009 ; Conner & Schmid 2003 ) and interacts with several actin - binding proteins ( Orth et al . 2002 ; Kessels et al . 2001 ; Jeng & Welch 2001 ) ; previous to this work , dynamin has not been investigated in association with fluorescein internalisation . These data suggest dynamin and its associated actin binding proteins are directly involved and contribute to the active internalisation of fluorescein by the cell . It was also found that metabolic activity is unaffected by treatment with dynasore , in line with earlier findings 155 that only viable cells can mediate fluorescein uptake . However , as fluorescein uptake was not completely inhibited by dynasore , it is possibly that other endocytic or active pathways independent of dynamin may contribute to some extent to uptake . Finally , this work examined which components of the two MPS which increase fluorescein uptake may be responsible for increasing the active internalisation of fluorescein . Previous studies of MPS - associated hyperfluorescence focus on the effects of biocides . However in this work , the potential hyperfluorescence - inducing effects of surfactants were investigated . The non - ionic surfactant Tetronic 1107 is common to both MPS associated with increased hyperfluorescence , but is not present in the two MPS that do not increase fluorescein uptake . It was observed that hyperfluorescence intensity increases significantly after treatment with 1 % ( w / v ) Tetronic 1107 ( the concentration found in P - PQ - 1107 and P - 1107 ) , and in L929 cells reaches a comparable level to that found after both P - PQ1 - 1107 and P - 1107 treatment . A smaller increase in fluorescein uptake was also found for L929 cells treated with 0 . 1 % and 10 % Tetronic 1107 . These data suggest Tetronic 1107 plays a key role in the hyperfluorescence caused by these MPS . Tetronic 1107 typically forms polymeric micelles which are more stable and less damaging to the lipid bilayer when compared to the typical surfactant micelle ( Sandez - Macho et al . 2015 ) . Tetronic 1107 , at all concentrations tested , caused no significant change in metabolic activity , consistent with other reports ( Rey - Rico et al . 2011 ) . Tetronics are also otherwise known as block copolymers . As polymeric micelles can readily encapsulate and solubilise otherwise poorly water - soluble drugs , block copolymers are widely studied for their drug delivery properties ( Alakhov et al . 1996 ; Harada & Kataoka 1998 ; Cammas et al . 1997 ) . The internalisation pathway of polymeric micelles and associated drug compounds remains unclear in the literature . However , a number of studies report polymeric micelle uptake is time - , pH - , energy - , and temperature - dependent ( Allen et al . 1999 ; Luo et al . 2002 ) , and report 156 localisation to several cytoplasmic organelles ( Savic et al . 2003 ) . Interestingly , it has been proposed that polymeric micelle uptake is also mediated by endocytosis ( Allen et al . 1999 ; Luo et al . 2002 ; Savic et al . 2003 ) . This finding that Tetronic 1107 may be responsible for MPS stimulation of fluorescein hyperfluorescence , may therefore be directly linked to the evidence for the role of dynamin - dependent processes ( which include endocytosis ) as a key mediator of fluorescein hyperfluorescence . In contrast , the surfactant Triton X - 100 does not induce increased fluorescein uptake in HC cells when used at levels above its CMC . These data suggest the mechanism for Tetronic 1107 induced hyperfluorescence may be specific to this block copolymer , and cannot be replicated with the similarly non - ionic surfactant Triton X - 100 . Triton X - 100 is often used to permeate cell membranes for protein extraction and prolonged exposure to this surfactant is known to cause lysis ( Koley & Bard 2010 ) . Thus it is perhaps unsurprising that also above its CMC , a significant decrease in metabolic activity is observed , which may counteract any increase in hyperfluorescence , once again in line with previous findings that non - viable and non - metabolically active cells exhibit minimal hyperfluorescence . Although PHMB - based MPS in most cases are associated with ocular staining ( as seen in the Andrasko Corneal Staining Grid ; www . staininggrid . com ) , in light of these current findings , the surfactant present may perhaps be more predicative of clinical hyperfluorescence . This study is the first to investigate the effects of surfactants on fluorescein uptake , and these findings suggest that hyperfluorescence could be attributed to the surfactant component in MPS formulations . Although interactions of the other MPS components in these solutions and the presence of a contact lens may contribute to the overall hyperfluorescence , these data suggest Tetronic 1107 or other surfactant effects on 157 active uptake processes in the cells is central to SICS . More broadly these findings suggest that active dynamin - dependent processes may be a key component of corneal fluorescein hyperfluorescence caused by a variety of stimuli . 5 . 6 . Conclusions These findings suggest that increased fluorescein hyperfluorescence is a marker for healthy metabolically active cells , and the absence of fluorescein staining is indicative of cytotoxicity . The uptake of fluorescein into the cell body appears to involve dynamin - associated processes . Increased fluorescein hyperfluorescence after MPS exposure is associated with the surfactant Tetronic 1107 , especially when present at 1 % ( w / v ) . This in vitro model might be used to screen potential solution formulations and components to predict fluorescein staining on the ocular surface , and to also investigate their implications on corneal health . 158 Chapter 6 Investigation of active transport mechanisms contributing to fluorescein hyperfluorescence and of the chemical effects of biocides on fluorescein uptake 159 6 . 1 . Abstract Purpose : To investigate receptor mediated uptake , mitochondrial oxidative phosphorylation and bulk fluid endocytosis as novel biological mechanisms contributing to hyperfluorescence in cell culture , and to explore the chemical effects of biocides on cell viability and fluorescein uptake . Methods : L929 cells were treated with oxidative phosphorylation uncoupler DNP and fluorescein to evaluate the effect of increased metabolic activity ( and loss of ATP production ) on fluorescein uptake . Receptor mediated uptake in murine fibroblasts was assessed by starving cells of serum overnight before treating with 0 . 01 % w / v fluorescein . Fluorescein uptake was then quantified in both instances using high content analysis ( HCA ) . A further biological mechanism investigated was macropinocytosis in both L929 and human corneal ( HC ) cells . Fluorescein uptake and FITC - conjugated dextran uptake ( a marker used to identify macropinocytosis ) was assessed in MPS treated human corneal ( HC ) cells using fluorescence microscopy . Similarly , pHRodo® Red Dextran , MPS and EIPA ( a macropinocytosis inhibitor ) were used to investigate fluorescein uptake by macropinocytosis in L929 cells . Finally , the effect of the biocides PHMB and PQ - 1 on cell viability was tested at concentrations present in the test MPS formulations used throughout this work , and their impact on hyperfluorescence was evaluated using HCA . Results : Fluorescein uptake was unaffected by overnight serum starvation and by DNP treatment . Macropinocytosis was not increased by hyperfluorescence - inducing MPS , but surprisingly was found to be elevated by those MPS that have not been found to increase hyperfluorescence ( PQ1 - Alex - 904 and PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 ) . This was further confirmed with the finding that the macropinocytosis inhibitor EIPA did not reduce hyperfluorescence after P - PQ1 - 1107 treatment . PHMB and PQ - 1 both caused a large decrease in metabolic 160 activity for all concentrations tested , and was reflected by limited fluorescein uptake across all biocide concentrations tested . Conclusions : Mitochondrial oxidative phosphorylation is not required for fluorescein uptake , and the lack of effect of serum starvation on fluorescein uptake suggests fluorescein uptake is unlikely to be a specific receptor - mediated endocytic process . In association with hyperfluorescence inducing MPS , macropinocytosis does not contribute to increased fluorescein uptake after MPS - treatment . Finally the biocides PHMB and PQ - 1 alone do not appear to be the components responsible for mediating fluorescein uptake in hyperfluorescence inducing MPS formulations ( confirming once again that cells do not show increased fluorescein uptake similar to those hyperfluorescence inducing formulations in response to a toxic stimulus ) . 161 6 . 2 . Introduction Sodium fluorescein ( ‘fluorescein’ ) has many applications , with these exploiting its fluorescent properties . Uses include determining skin damage in fish ( Livengood et al . 2013 ) , detecting trace amounts of blood in forensic science ( Cheeseman & Dimeo 1995 ; Martin & Cahill 2004 ) and an ocular surface diagnostic tool in ophthalmology . In particular , fluorescein is used to assess conjunctival and corneal integrity ( Lofstrom 2005 ; Dumbleton 2002 ; Holden et al . 2001 ) by topically applying a small volume of an aqueous solution of fluorescein ( 1mg / ml or 2mg / ml ) to the ocular surface . Staining of the ocular surface ( ‘hyperfluorescence’ ) is conventionally interpreted to be indicative of poor ocular health ( G . Wilson et al . 1995 ; Tabery 1992 ; Tabery 2003a ; Tabery 2003b ) . One type of hyperfluorescence often seen in practice occurs with certain soft contact lens and multi - purpose solutions ( MPS ) combinations known as solution induced corneal staining ( SICS ) ( Andrasko & Ryen 2008 ; Carnt , Willcox , et al . 2007 ; L . Jones et al . 2002 ) . Although some progress has been made in underpinning the biological and chemical basis of SICS , the precise mechanism ( s ) for fluorescein uptake and hyperfluorescence inducing activities of major MPS components are yet to be defined . There are a number of hypotheses proposed for hyperfluorescence on the ocular surface . It has previously been suggested that fluorescein pools in the impressions of the epithelial tissue and in the tear film which results in an increase in observed hyperfluorescence ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . Another proposed mechanism is that hyperfluorescence is the increase in fluorescein moving freely throughout the spaces between cells referred to as the ingress model ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . A hypothesis that has been investigated more recently is that fluorescein taken into epithelial cells and hyperfluorescence reflects the internalisation of fluorescein in the cell body ( Mokhtarzadeh et al . 2011 ; Bakkar et al . 2014 ; Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) . 162 MPS are sterile single - use formulations used to disinfect and store re - usable contact lenses . A number of studies report cytotoxic effects of certain contact lens solutions ( Choy et al . 2012 ; Wright & Mowrey - McKee 2005 ; Dutot et al . 2008 ; Dutot et al . 2010 ) . It is suggested that hyperfluorescence associated with the use of certain MPS is a result of cellular damage although two previous studies suggest SICS does not reflect cytotoxicity ( Tchao et al . 2002 ; Bakkar et al . 2014 ) . In Chapter 5 , using propidium iodide ( PI ) ( a fluorescent necrosis marker ) and metabolic activity assays , it was demonstrated that two MPS associated with minimal hyperfluorescence clinically , similarly result in minimal hyperfluorescence in cell culture and also cause necrosis . Conversely , two MPS typically associated with an increase in hyperfluorescence clinically also caused hyperfluorescence in cell culture , though with minimal necrosis . It has further been suggested that hyperfluorescence is an indicator of apoptosis ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) . A study by Bandamwar and colleagues ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) demonstrated an increase in hyperfluorescence in apoptotic human corneal limbal epithelial ( HCLE ) cells . Apoptosis in this study was identified by localisation of fluorescence of the apoptosis marker Annexin V tagged with a red fluorophore in cells also treated with red fluorescent necrosis marker PI . However , ‘background’ staining of PI may have interfered with the red fluorescence observed for Annexin V , making it difficult to measure any genuine apoptosis . This is in contrast to the findings in Chapter 5 , where murine fibroblasts treated with both hyperfluorescence inducing and non - hyperfluorescence inducing MPS did not exhibit markers of apoptosis above that of the control . A study from this laboratory previously reported that fluorescein uptake and release is temperature dependent and thus involves active transport ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) . By definition , active transport mechanisms ( including endocytosis and exocytosis ) are energy dependent , ATP requiring processes . The compound 2 , 4 - dinitrophenol ( DNP ) is known to 163 increase metabolic rate ( Vaughan et al . 2012 ; Scheindlin 2008 ) by uncoupling oxidative phosphorylation and reducing ATP synthesis ( Desquiret et al . 2006 ; Joel et al . 1967 ; Sibille et al . 1995 ) . To investigate the relationship between hyperfluorescence and active transport mechanisms , fluorescein uptake in DNP - treated cells was additionally measured . As also previously shown in Chapter 5 , fluorescein uptake is associated with dynamin - mediated processes , a GTP - ase protein that has been implicated in a number of endocytic pathways ( Doherty & McMahon 2009 ) . After treatment with those MPS associated with increased hyperfluorescence ( P - PQ1 - 1107 and P - 1107 ) and dynasore ( a dynamin inhibitor ) in both murine fibroblasts and HC cells , a significant decrease in fluorescein uptake was observed . However hyperfluorescence is not entirely dependent on these processes suggesting that other routes of fluorescein uptake exist . Receptor - mediated endocytosis is also an energy dependent process , where molecules such as transferrin and lipoproteins complexes ( for example low density lipoproteins [ LDL ] ) are internalised when bound to unique receptors on the cell surface ( Schwartz 1995 ; Ciechanover et al . 1983 ) . Serum ( fetal bovine serum [ FBS ] or fetal calf serum [ FCS ] ) , which is a key constituent of cell culture medium , contains such proteins and growth factors . Various aspects of cell growth and physiology contribute to the distribution of receptors in cells ( Ciechanover et al . 1983 ) . For example , transferrin in serum - supplemented growth medium may affect the number ( J . H . Ward et al . 1982 ) and distribution ( Klausner et al . 1983 ) of transferrin receptors . Serum is thus often omitted or used at a much lower concentration when preparing cell cultures for uptake assays so as not to influence the overall endocytic measurement ( Soraj et al . 2012 ; Commisso et al . 2014 ; Fielding et al . 2012 ; Hernaez & Alonso 2010 ) . To investigate whether fluorescein is internalised via receptor - mediated endocytosis , hyperfluorescence was measured in cells cultured in serum free media . The assumption was that following maintenance under serum - free conditions , any receptors being utilised by fluorescein 164 would not be blocked by any competing serum - component . Thus should receptor - mediated uptake occur , a higher fluorescein uptake for serum - free maintained cells would be expected relative to cells grown in the presence of growth medium containing serum . A further biological mechanism studied in this work was macropinocytosis , the bulk uptake of fluids from the extracellular environment . Although macropinocytosis is a dynamin independent process , it has been shown that dynasore can prevent membrane ruffling typical of this uptake mechanism ( Preta et al . 2015 ) . Therefore , in this study macropinocytosis as an additional pathway for fluorescein entry into cell in the absence of dynamin inhibitor ( dynasore ) was investigated . Dextran is frequently used as a marker molecule for macropinocytosis ( Falcone et al . 2006 ) , and so the relative effects of FITC - conjugated dextran ( 10kDa ) uptake in MPS treated cells were measured . Additionally , the chemical 5 - ( N - ethyl - N - isopropyl ) amiloride ( EIPA ) , a more potent analogue of the well - known macropinocytosis inhibitor Amiloride ( Meier et al . 2002 ; West et al . 1989 ) , was used to investigate whether inhibition of macropinocytosis might reduce fluorescein uptake . It is noteworthy that previous to this study , receptor - mediated uptake , macropinocytosis and the effect of oxidative phosphorylation on hyperfluorescence have not been investigated as biological mechanisms underpinning MPS induced fluorescein . MPS formulations typically comprise a number of generic classes of compounds , including surfactants ( for example Tetronics® ) , biocides such as PHMB and Polyquaternium - 1 ( PQ - 1 ) and buffers ( borate , phosphate or citrate ) . In addition to the further studies of the mechanism underlying hyperfluorescence , the potential importance of MPS biocides in mediating the ability of MPS to increase hyperfluorescence was also investigated . Current applications of the broad spectrum antimicrobial PHMB ( Carmona - Ribeiro & de Melo Carrasco 2013 ) range from swimming pool sanitation ( Kusnetsov et al . 1997 ) to use as an 165 anti - microbial mouthwash ( Rosin et al . 2001 ) . PHMB also acts against some fungi and protozoa where it is typically used to treat Acanthamoeba keratitis ( Gray et al . 1994 ) . PQ - 1 , a quaternary ammonium compound related to the preservative BKC , again primarily acts against bacteria with reports of limited activity against Acanthamoeba castellanii ( Codling et al . 2003 ) . Biocides are often considered to be the main hyperfluorescence - inducing component in an MPS formulation . Indeed , Andrasko and colleagues report that clinical hyperfluorescence increases with those MPS containing biocide PHMB ; this is presented in the Andrasko Staining Grid ( accessible at www . staininggrid . com ) . Similarly , Carnt et al have demonstrated an increase in clinical hyperfluorescence with biocide PQ - 1 based solutions ( Carnt , Willcox , et al . 2007 ) . However , using an in vitro model it was previously demonstrated in Chapter 5 that fluorescein uptake is induced in solutions containing Tetronic 1107 , a non - ionic surfactant found in hyperfluorescence - inducing MPS . It was also reported that only metabolically active and viable cells exhibit increased hyperfluorescence ( Chapter 5 ) . Therefore , in this study fluorescein uptake a result of MPS biocide induced cytotoxicity in cell culture was investigated . Interestingly , clinical hyperfluorescence is often reported as the result of the biocide component in an MPS , although the ability of individual biocides to cause hyperfluorescence at concentrations relevant to those found in MPS formulations has not been directly investigated ; thus in this work , biocides were investigated at concentrations relevant to those found in four different MPS , two of which are associated with clinical hyperfluorescence . To summarise , using the unique in vitro model developed in this thesis , the purpose of this study was to a ) study active transport processes including receptor - mediated uptake and macropinocytosis as biological mechanisms underpinning hyperfluorescence and ( b ) investigate the relationship between cellular viability and fluorescein uptake as an effect of MPS biocides PQ - 1 and PHMB . 166 6 . 3 . Methods and Materials Cell culture 6 . 3 . 1 . HC cells were obtained from human corneal explants provided by Manchester Eye Bank . Briefly , HC were grown from segmented sections of corneal explants in wells pre - coated for 1 hour with 0 . 01 % calf - skin type I collagen ( Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) in Dulbecco’s PBS ( PBS ) ( ThermoFisher , UK ) . This protocol was adapted from Kahn et al , 1994 ( Kahn et al . 1993 ) . Murine fibroblasts ( L929 cells ) ( ECACC , UK ) and HC cells were maintained at 37°C and 5 % CO 2 with Dulbecco’s Modified Eagle Medium ( DMEM ) containing 4500mg - L glucose ( Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) supplemented with 10 % v / v fetal bovine serum ( FBS ) ( Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) and 4mM L - glutamine ( Gibco by Life Technologies , UK ) , referred to hereafter as ‘growth medium’ . For HC cells , all tissue culture flasks and plates had been pre - coated for 1 hour with 0 . 01 % calf - skin type I collagen in PBS . Both cell types were maintained until growth had reached approximately 80 % confluency , and were then rinsed with PBS and treated with 0 . 25 % trypsin - EDTA ( Life Technologies , UK ) for L929 cells or 0 . 05 % trypsin - EDTA in PBS for HC cells . After cell detachment trypsin - EDTA was neutralised by addition of equal volumes of growth medium . For experiments , cells were seeded in 24 - well plates ( Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) at a density of 1x10 5 cell / well for fluorescence microscopy or in 96 well plates ( Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) at 2 . 5x10 4 cells / well for high content analysis ( HCA ) or cell viability experiments using growth medium . In all cases cells were used in experiments after overnight growth . In the instance of serum starvation , L929 cells were cultured overnight using FBS free growth medium . Cell treatment with MPS 6 . 3 . 2 . MPS formulations were obtained commercially based on their differential association with clinical fluorescein hyperfluorescence , and their main biocide and surfactant components . Cells were treated with MPS formulations for 2 hours at 100 % v / v concentration . MPS investigated which are known to cause hyperfluorescence were : ReNu Sensitive Multi - 167 purpose solution® ( Bausch + Lomb ) referred to as P - 1107 and Biotrue® ( Bausch + Lomb ) referred to as P - PQ1 - 1107 . MPS investigated which do not cause hyperfluorescence were : Complete RevitaLens® ( AMO ) referred to as PQ1 - Alex - 904 and Opti - Free Replenish® ( Alcon ) referred to as PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 . The main biocide and surfactant components in these MPS can be seen in Table 14 . Effects were compared with cells treated for 2 hours with growth medium ( media control ) , or borate buffer ( carrier control ) . Borate buffer was prepared using 0 . 6 % boric acid and 0 . 1 % borax in distilled water . Table 14 : MPS formulations . Cell treatment with fluorescein 6 . 3 . 3 . After treatment with test solutions / MPS formulations , cells were incubated with 0 . 01 % w / v fluorescein ( Fluorescein Sodium salt ; Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) in PBS for 10 minutes at 37°C . Hoechst 33342 ( Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) , at a final concentration of 0 . 2mg / ml in PBS , was added to each well to enable identification of all the nuclei in each cell population as required for high content analysis ( described below in Section 6 . 3 . 8 ) . On removal from the incubator , cells were kept cold and washed three times with cold PBS . It was previously MPS Manufacturer Biocide ( s ) Surfactant Biotrue P - PQ1 - 1107 Bausch + Lomb Polyquartenium - 1 ( 0 . 0001 % ) , PHMB ( 0 . 00013 % ) Tetronic® 1107 ( 1 . 0 % ) ReNu Sensitive P - 1107 Bausch + Lomb PHMB ( 0 . 00005 % ) Tetronic® 1107 ( 1 . 0 % ) Opti - free Replenish PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 Alcon Polyquaternium - 1 ( 0 . 001 % ) , ALDOX ( 0 . 0005 % ) Tetronic® 1304 ( 0 . 05 % ) Complete Revitalens PQ1 - Alex - 904 AMO Polyquaternium - 1 ( 0 . 0003 % ) , Alexidine dihydrochloride ( 0 . 00016 % ) Tetronic® 904 ( 0 . 1 % ) 168 shown that use of cold temperature for observation of treated cells was necessary to prevent efflux of fluorescein over time ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) . Cells were kept on ice until high content analysis ( HCA ) or fluorescence microscopy with this being carried out within 5 minutes from the end of treatment ( described in Sections 6 . 3 . 8 and 6 . 3 . 9 respectively ) . Cell treatment with DNP 6 . 3 . 4 . L929 cells were treated with a 100µM solution of 2 , 4 - dinitrophenol ( DNP ; Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) prepared in growth medium and 10 % DMSO to aid compound solubilisation . For cell treatment , media was removed from each well after overnight growth and 100µM DNP was added for 15 minutes at 37°C . Effects on cell metabolic activity were then compared with cells treated with growth medium only ( media control ) . Cell treatment with FITC - dextran , EIPA , and pHRodo 6 . 3 . 5 . Fluorescein isothiocyanite ( FITC ) conjugated dextran ( 10000 MW ; Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) was used as a fluid - phase marker to identify macropinosomes in L929 cells treated with test MPS formulations . After treatment with media or MPS formulations as described in 6 . 3 . 2 , FITC - dextran was prepared in PBS and added to cells at a final concentration of 0 . 5mg / ml for 10 minutes at 37°C . Cells were then washed three times with cold PBS , and kept cold prior to fluorescence microscopy ( described in Section 6 . 3 . 9 ) . In subsequent experiments , the effect of fluorescein uptake in HC cells treated with macropinocytosis inhibitor 5 - ( N - Ethyl - N - Isopropyl ) - Amiloride ( EIPA ; Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) was investigated . A solution of 50µM EIPA was prepared in growth medium and 0 . 06 % DMSO . HC cells were treated with MPS P - PQ1 - 1107 for 2 hours at 100 % v / v and then 50µM EIPA for 30 minutes at 37°C . To detect macropinocytosis , pHRodo® Red Dextran ( Molecular Probes® by Life Technologies , UK ) prepared in Live Cell Imaging Solution ( Molecular Probes® by Life Technologies , UK ) was then added to cells at a final concentration of 20µg / ml for 10 minutes at the same time as fluorescein addition . Cells 169 were subsequently washed three times with cold PBS , and kept cold prior to fluorescence microscopy ( described in Section 6 . 3 . 9 ) . Fluorescein uptake and extent of macropinocytosis in EIPA treated cells were compared to cells treated with P - PQ1 - 1107 only . Cell treatment with MPS components 6 . 3 . 6 . In later experiments , L929 cells were treated for 2 hours at 37°C with 0 . 00005 % , 0 . 00013 % and 0 . 001 % w / v solutions of Cosmocil® CQ PHMB ( Lonza , USA ) , and 0 . 00001 % , 0 . 0001 % , 0 . 0003 % and 0 . 001 % w / v solutions of Polyquaternium - 1 ( PQ - 1 ; Stratech Scientific Ltd , UK ) prepared in borate buffer . Cells were then treated with 0 . 01 % w / v fluorescein as described in Section 6 . 3 . 3 and fluorescein uptake was quantified using HCA as descibed in Section 6 . 3 . 8 . Metabolic activity assays ( MTT ) 6 . 3 . 7 . Cells growing in 96 well plates were treated with test formulations , before aspiration and replacement with media containing 0 . 5mg / ml thiazolyl blue tetrazolium bromide ( MTT ) ( Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) , and subsequent incubation for 2 hours at 37°C . Media containing MTT was then aspirated , and insoluble formazan was solubilised using 100µl of DMSO ( Sigma - Aldrich , UK ) , followed by assessment of absorbance at 555nm . High content analysis ( HCA ) 6 . 3 . 8 . Quantification of fluorescein uptake was carried out using the Cellomics Array Scan VTI HCS Reader , and the accompanying HCS Studio Cell 2 . 0 Analysis Software . Cells were visualised using the ArrayScan ™ automated Observer Z1 inverted microscope ( Zeiss ) with transmitted light and fluorescence using an XF53 filter wheel . High - resolution images were taken using a CCD camera ( Hamamatsu Orca ER ) with a 5x / 0 . 25 Fluar objective . Images of fluorescein stained cells were taken using 0 . 033 seconds exposure for all experiments . One field of view was taken per well , with multiple wells per treatment tested to enable quick data collection . Samples were incubated at 4°C as they were imaged to 170 limit fluorescein loss from cells . Using a built in bioapplication and adjusted for cell type , the mean pixel intensity of each cell was measured per treatment . The median fluorescence intensity value was then reported in Arbitrary Units ( AU ) ( median ( lower 95 % CI limit - upper 95 % CI limit ) ) . Fluorescence microscopy 6 . 3 . 9 . Widefield fluorescent images were collected on an Olympus IX83 inverted microscope using a 10x / 0 . 3 UPlanFL N , or 20x / 0 . 45 LUC PlanFL N ( Ph1 ) objective and captured using an Orca ER camera ( Hamamatsu ) through CellSens software ( Olympus ) . All images were acquired sequentially and using the appropriate filters to ensure no bleed through the channels . Images were processed using ImageJ software . Statistical analysis 6 . 3 . 10 . All fluorescein fluorescence intensity data are presented as the median ( lower 95 % confidence interval ( CI ) – upper limit 95 % CI ) , where error bars represent 95 % CI . Metabolic activities are presented as a percentage of the appropriate control and the associated 95 % CI , calculated using the median metabolic activity values . All data were analysed using non - parametric Kruskal - Wallis ANOVA and Dunn’s multiple comparison post - hoc tests unless otherwise stated . The level of statistical analysis was set to * p = 0 . 05 , * * p = 0 . 01 and * * * p ≤ 0 . 001 for all tests . 6 . 4 . Results Investigation of biological mechanisms underpinning hyperfluorescence 6 . 4 . 1 . Fluorescein uptake is unaffected by DNP , an oxidative phosphorylation 6 . 4 . 1 . 1 . uncoupler Initially the effect of DNP treatment on fluorescein uptake by L929 cells were examined . L929 cells treated with DNP exhibited a statistically significant increase in metabolic activity relative to media control ( 130 . 5 % ( 110 . 5 - 149 . 6 % ; p = 0 . 04 ) ( n = 8 wells for both treatments ) suggesting a successful uncoupling of oxidative phosphorylation . A large but 171 statistically non - significant decrease in metabolic activity was observed with BKC ( which is known to cause necrosis ) ( n = 6 wells ) ( 3 . 4 % ( 2 . 4 - 3 . 8 % ) p = 0 . 14 ; Figure 37 ) . The mean number of cells after treatment with media control was 607 cells ( 505 - 709 cells ) ( n = 3 wells ) whereas the mean number of cells treated after treatment with DNP decreased to 317 cells ( 267 - 366 cells ) ( n = 3 wells ) . The median fluorescein intensities and associated lower 95 % CI – upper 95 % CI ( reported in AU ) measured with media control and DNP treatments were 13 . 91 ( 13 . 8 - 14 ) and 14 . 3 ( 14 . 2 - 14 . 4 ) respectively ( Figure 38 ) . Using the Mann - Whitney statistical test , the fluorescence intensity after DNP treatment was statistically greater than that exhibited by media control treated cells ( p < 0 . 0001 ) , however this difference ( and associated 95 % CI ) was extremely small ( 0 . 41 ( 0 . 40 - 0 . 60 ) . The data set acquired for fluorescein fluorescence ( Figure 38 ) is much larger than that collected for metabolic activity ( Figure 37 ) . For example , due to the nature of each assay , an average of 317 cells , and thus an average of 317 fluorescence intensity data points , were collected for DNP treated cells in comparison to 8 data points of absorbance values in similarly DNP treated cells . Therefore , it is likely that this accounts for the statistically significant increase in fluorescence intensity , although small , ( Figure 38 ) compared to the large , yet statistically less significant , change in metabolic activity ( Figure 37 ) . More importantly , the statistical significance calculated for fluorescence intensity values are unlikely to be related to the statistically significant increase exhibited in metabolic activity . Thus , it is unlikely that fluorescein uptake is affected by small increases in metabolic activity ( and the associated loss of ATP production ) induced by DNP . 172 Figure 37 : Effect of DNP and BKC on L929 cell metabolic activity ( n = 8 wells in both instances ) . L929 cells were grown overnight in serum free media before fluorescein treatment to investigate receptor - mediated uptake as a potential mechanism of fluorescein uptake . All fluorescein intensity values are reported as the median fluorescence intensity in Arbitrary Units ( AU ) and associated lower 95 % CI - upper 95 % CI . Fluorescein uptake in L929 cells treated overnight with serum free media was not statistically different to that demonstrated by overnight treatment with media control ( 439 . 7 ( 427 - 450 . 2 ) and 401 . 7 ( 355 . 6 - 450 ) respectively ; p = 0 . 77 ) . This suggests fluorescein uptake is unlikely to be a receptor - mediated process . As expected , an increase in fluorescein uptake was observed in L929 cells treated with MPS formulations P - PQ1 - 1107 and P - 1107 and minimal fluorescence intensities were measured in PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 and PQ1 - Alex - 904 treated cells compared to media control ( p < 0 . 0001 in all instances ) . Similarly , the same trend in fluorescence intensities was also observed in comparison to serum free media treated cells ( p < 0 . 0001 in all instances ) . To confirm that macropinocytosis was not associated with increased hyperfluorescence , fluorescein uptake was tested in L929 cells treated with hyperfluorescence inducing MPS P - PQ1 - 1107 and macropinocytosis inhibitor EIPA . Using pHRodo® Red Dextran as a marker for macropinocytosis , it was confirmed that EIPA decreased macropinosome formation as seen by the loss of red fluorescence in Figure 41D . However , on fluorescein addition to P - PQ1 - 1107 and EIPA treated cells , no change in fluorescein uptake was observed as seen by the extent of green fluorescence apparent in Figure 41F compared to cells treated with P - PQ1 - 1107 only ( Figure 41E ) . These data together suggest increased fluorescein uptake caused by hyperfluorescence inducing MPS is not a macropinocytosis associated process . Investigation of biocides as chemical inducers of hyperfluorescence 6 . 4 . 3 . PQ - 1 induces a decrease in L929 cell metabolic activity 6 . 4 . 3 . 1 . The metabolic activity of PQ - 1 and fluorescein treated cells are presented relative to the metabolic activity of cells treated with media control ( Figure 42 ) . A large but statistically non - significant decrease in metabolic activity was seen with 0 . 00001 % , 0 . 0001 % and 0 . 0003 % PQ - 1 + FL treatments ( 25 . 4 % ( 23 . 1 - 26 . 9 % ) ; p > 0 . 9999 , 9 . 4 % ( 7 . 1 - 14 . 3 % ) ; p = 0 . 12 and 21 . 6 % ( 19 . 2 - 24 . 4 % ) ; p = 0 . 73 respectively ) . As expected , the metabolic activity of media control + FL cells was comparable to media control treated cells ( 86 . 9 % ( 84 . 7 - 106 . 1 % ) ; p > 0 . 9999 ) . Given that a decrease in metabolic activity was observed in cells identically treated with PQ - 1 ( Section 6 . 4 . 3 ) , it is perhaps unsurprising that these data indicate that PQ - 1 alone cannot cause the levels of hyperfluorescence typically observed with P - PQ1 - 1107 . It is also unlikely to be the only component that causes the loss of hyperfluorescence associated with PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 and PQ1 - Alex - 904 . Fluorescein uptake in cells treated with PHMB ( at all concentrations ) were statistically less than that demonstrated by cells treated with hyperfluorescence inducing formulations P - PQ1 - 1107 and P - 1107 , but were greater than that exhibited by cells treated with formulations PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 and PQ1 - Alex - 904 ( p < 0 . 0001 in all instances ) . The minimal hyperfluorescence observed with PHMB treatments is in line with the decrease in metabolic activities measured ( as seen in Section 6 . 4 . 3 . 2 ) and with previous finding that 182 only metabolically active cells exhibit increased hyperfluorescence . These data strongly indicate that PHMB alone cannot cause the levels of hyperfluorescence typically observed with P - 1107 or P - PQ1 - 1107 . Discussion Various biological and chemical triggers of hyperfluorescence were investigated to improve understanding of clinical ocular staining . In previous work it was found that hyperfluorescence is a mechanism associated with GTP - ase dynamin , which has been implicated in a number of ATP - requiring endocytic processes . This in line with earlier findings from this laboratory which show that fluorescein uptake is an active and energy dependent process ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) . However , hyperfluorescence appeared not to be dependent on dynamin - associated mechanisms alone , and so the ATP requirement of fluorescein uptake mechanisms using DNP as well as receptor - mediated endocytosis and macropinocytosis as further biological mechanism of fluorescein uptake were explored . Given that a number of studies implicate biocides as the components responsible , in this work the hyperfluorescence inducing abilities of biocides PHMB and PQ - 1 as an effect of their respective cytotoxicity capabilities was also studied . Fluorescein internalisation as a function of metabolic activity and ATP production was investigated in L929 cells . Cells treated with DNP indeed demonstrated an increase in metabolic activity as seen in Figure 37 , suggesting a successful uncoupling of oxidative phosphorylation . In brief , DNP acts a protonophore moving protons across lipid bilayers . This creates a leak in the inner mitochondrial membrane destroying the proton gradient and bypasses the requirement for ATP - synthase and consequently , energy from the gradient is dissipated as heat instead of generating ATP ( Desquiret et al . 2006 ; Joel et al . 1967 ; Sibille et al . 1995 ) . DNP is used in a range of disciplines . For example , it has been used to explore metabolic rates in bobwhite quails ( Dominguez et al . 1993 ) and in skeletal muscle cells ( Vaughan et al . 2012 ) , to inhibit bacterial adhesion to surfaces ( Paul 1984 ; Jain et al . 2007 ) and has recently been discovered to be a neuroprotective compound ( Freitas - Correa et al . 2013 ) . It is nevertheless best known for its ability to reversibly inhibit the coupling of oxygen uptake to phosphorylation and generation of high - energy phosphate bonds , first 184 described by Loomis and Lipmann ( Loomis & Lipmann 1948 ) . The chemical DNP was commonly used as a weight loss drug in the 1930’s and became known as a treatment for obesity . However due to increasing reports of serious side effects ( for example , hepatic / renal damage and ‘dinitrophenol cataracts’ ) , the substance was banned in 1938 from further use ( Colman 2007 ) . Although previously MPS were assumed to cause hyperfluorescence due to their toxicity , this laboratory previously demonstrated cellular activity is fundamental for fluorescein hyperfluorescence ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) . However the loss of ATP production associated with DNP treatment studied here did not have an effect on cellular hyperfluorescence , and the median fluorescence intensity of DNP treated L929 cells was similar to that exhibited by the media control ( Figure 38 ) . This was also despite the loss of cells with DNP treatment . These data suggest that an ATP requirement for fluorescein uptake is not rate limiting . Indeed , varied energy requirements for the uptake of large and small particle containing vesicles into peritoneal macrophages have been reported by Casley - Smith ( 1969 ) . Inhibiting cell activity with low temperatures and metabolic poisons ( such as DNP ) was seen to prevent cells internalising large , and even groups of small , particles and vesicles ; the uptake of small particles into vesicles and the subsequent internalisation into cells was however unaffected ( Casley Smith 1969 ) . The metabolic activity of DNP treated cells in this instance could not be measured alongside fluorescein quantification and the exact increase in metabolic activity and loss in ATP production is unknown . In future work , the ATP production of DNP and media control treated cells could be investigated more closely using , and quantified , for example , using a luciferase assay . This would also perhaps provide insight into the size of vesicles fluorescein is utilising during internalisation . 185 L929 cell cultures were also grown overnight in serum free media and subsequently treated with 0 . 01 % w / v fluorescein to study receptor - mediated uptake as a biological mechanism of hyperfluorescence . Fluorescein uptake in serum free media treated cells however was not comparable to cells treated with formulations associated with increased fluorescein uptake nor the formulations associated with minimal fluorescein uptake ( Figure 39 ) . Most significantly , little change was seen in the median fluorescein intensity of serum free media treated cells when compared to media control . Given that endocytic assays typically utilise cell cultures starved of serum to maximise receptor - mediated uptake of the components being measured , these data suggest uptake of hyperfluorescence may be unrelated to receptor - mediated endocytic process . It was not presumed that fluorescein binds to a ‘fluorescein specific’ receptor , but rather that it may be capable of binding to receptors which are available for other naturally - occurring ligands . In a broader biological context , indeed a large number of atypical ligands act on receptors in a nonspecific manner , which impedes with the binding of the usual ligand of with the receptor ( Lalanne & Francois 2015 ; Mora 2015 ) . An example of this is immune ligand detection of a T - cell receptor , which must bind specific peptides from amongst a large number of non - specific peptides ( Dittel et al . 1999 ) . In future , inhibitors of receptor - mediated endocytosis ( exposure to hypertonicity , cytoplasmic acidification , phenylarsine oxide or primary amines ) and measurement of LDL uptake as described by Bradley and colleagues ( Bradley et al . 1993 ) could be used to study this mechanism of uptake further . These data nevertheless also strongly indicate that hyperfluorescence is most likely a consequence of specific interactions with MPS components or formulations . Notably , the differential responses in fluorescein uptake induced by MPS formulations could not be replicated with serum deprivation . In this in vitro model , cells undergo a 2 - hour treatment with MPS at 100 % concentration , in line with the transient SICS phenomenon where 186 maximum clinical staining is observed between 2 and 4 hours ( Garofalo et al . 2005 ) , or between 1 and 2 hours post lens wear ( Bandamwar et al . 2010 ) . It is also in keeping with clinical study of hyperfluorescence that was performed with multiple MPS and contact lens combinations by Andrasko and colleagues , seen in the Andrasko Corneal Staining Grid ( www . stainggrid . com ) . During this incubation step in this model , cells are devoid of proteins and various growth factors typically provided by serum supplemented growth medium . As seen in previous work in Chapter 5 , fluorescein uptake is dependent on cell viability . The primary functions of serum are to provide ( a ) growth factors and hormones for cell growth and proliferation ( b ) transport proteins carrying hormones , minerals , trace elements and lipids , ( c ) attachment and spreading factors such as the components of extracellular matrix and ( d ) stabilising and detoxifying factors needed to maintain pH or to inhibit proteases ( Gstraunthaler 2003 ) . By culturing cells in serum - free media it is possible that other cellular processes have also been affected in turn affecting cellular ability to mediate fluorescein uptake . Prolonged serum deprivation has indeed shown to induce apoptosis in various cell lines ( Rawson 1991 ; Lindenboim et al . 1995 ; Mills et al . 1998 ; Rühl et al . 1999 ; Kues et al . 2002 ; Kues et al . 2000 ) , and has seen to reduce cell survival and increase DNA fragmentation in bovine and porcine cell lines ( Gibbons et al , 2002 ) . It is typically used to induce quiescent status of donor cells for nuclear cloning however given that serum also reduces cell viability more desirable synchronisation methods are being investigated ( Hayes et al . 2005 ) . Nevertheless , the mean number of cells of serum starved cells were comparable to the mean number of cells cultured in serum - supplemented growth medium ( media control ) suggesting serum starvation did not have a detrimental effect on cell growth . Basal growth medium also contains other components that aid cell growth ; for example : glucose that is a primary source of energy , amino acids which are compulsory for 187 protein synthesis , vitamins acting as co - enzymes or prosthetic groups in cell metabolism processes , and inorganic salts which are required for cell growth ( Yang & Xiong 2012 ; Arora 2013 ) . To confirm this in the future however , cell viability measurements such as MTT assays or live / dead fluorescence microscopy assays ( using Hoechst 3342 and propidium iodide ) could be used . Bakkar et al demonstrated that fluorescein uptake is an energy dependent process ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) and previous findings in this thesis indicate that it is in part associated with dynamin - dependent processes ( Chapter 5 ) . Macropinocytosis is also an energy - dependent but dynamin - independent process for the uptake of fluids , and was investigated as an additional biological mechanism of hyperfluorescence . Markedly , in HC cells treated with hyperfluorescence inducing MPS , there was little evidence of macropinocytosis when investigated using FITC - dextran ( Figure 40 ) . These data suggest that fluorescein uptake associated with hyperfluorescence inducing MPS formulations is unrelated to macropinocytosis . This was additionally confirmed in EIPA and fluorescein treated L929 cells ( Figure 41 ) . However , with PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 and PQ1 - Alex - 904 , formulations associated with low levels of hyperfluorescence , an increase in dextran uptake above the media control was observed ( Figure 40 ) . Together these data suggest that macropinocytosis in this instance is affected by MPS but unrelated to fluorescein uptake . The visualisation and quantification of macropinosomes using fluorescently labelled dextran ( Saeed et al . 2010 ; J . T . H . Wang et al . 2010 ; Soraj et al . 2012 ) has been used to identify macropinocytosis as an important pathway that drives cancer cell proliferation and growth , and has been linked to the oncogene - stimulated internalisation of serum albumin ( Commisso et al . 2013 ; Commisso et al . 2014 ) . In this study , dextran with the molecular weight 10kDa in the forms of FITC - dextran and pHRodo® Red Dextran was used ( Figure 188 40 and Figure 41 respectively ) . There is some literature however that indicates size of dextran fluid - phase markers may influence their endocytic pathway . In particular , it is suggested that 70kDa dextran is a better probe for macropinocytosis whereas 10kDa ( or smaller ) sized dextran are better for general fluid - phase endocytosis ( both micropinocytosis and macropinocytosis ) ( L . Li et al . 2015 ) . However , having observed no change in fluorescein uptake in L929 cells treated with macropinocytosis inhibitor EIPA , these data strongly indicate hyperfluorescence is indeed unrelated to this pathway . To build on the findings in this study , in the future larger dextran molecules would be used in these macropinocytosis studies to ensure this specific endocytic pathway was accurately assessed . Furthermore , dextran and fluorescein uptake would be quantified by high content analysis to provide quantitative as well as qualitative information . The relationship of cellular viability and fluorescein uptake in biocide treated murine fibroblasts was next examined . Due to the association of increased clinical staining with PHMB containing MPS however , PHMB has often been implicated as the hyperfluorescence - inducing component in MPS . One study by Bandamwar and colleagues ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) demonstrated hyperfluorescence in human corneal limbal epithelial cells using 0 . 001 % w / v PHMB ( approximately 10 times the concentration typically found in MPS ) . PHMB has also been implicated in inducing hyperfluorescence by an alternative mechanism referred to as the preservative associated transient hyperfluorescence ( PATH ) hypothesis ( Bright et al . 2012 ) . This hypothesis suggests that PHMB adsorbs onto to corneal epithelial surface that mediates a secondary association of fluorescein molecules to the same sites ; the localisation of PHMB / fluorescein complexes on the cell surface is then observed as hyperfluorescence . Bright and colleagues nevertheless also argue that PQ - 1 may mediate fluorescein molecules to the cellular surface in a similar manner ( albeit exhibiting a weaker fluorescein signal than PHMB - 189 mediated fluorescein ) . This is in keeping with reports of clinical hyperfluorescence with PQ - 1 containing MPS formulations by Carnt and colleagues ( Carnt , Willcox , et al . 2007 ) . On investigating the metabolic activity and fluorescein uptake in L929 cell exposed to 0 . 0001 % w / v PQ - 1 ( the concentration in hyperfluorescence inducing MPS P - PQ1 - 1107 ) , the fluorescein intensity was not comparable to the levels of hyperfluorescence seen with P - PQ1 - 1107 ( Figure 44 ) . Similarly , at PHMB concentrations of 0 . 00005 % and 0 . 00013 % w / v , which are found in hyperfluorescence inducing formulations P - 1107 and P - PQ1 - 1107 respectively , fluorescein uptake was not comparable to those demonstrated by P - 1107 and P - PQ1 - 1107 ( Figure 45 ) . Moreover , given that the median fluorescence intensities of 0 . 00005 % and 0 . 00013 % w / v PHMB were very similar to that demonstrated by the carrier control borate buffer , it could be argued that the fluorescence observed is an effect of the carrier control alone . The fluorescein fluorescence intensity data acquired for PHMB and PQ - 1 treated cells at these concentrations are in keeping with our previous findings pertaining to metabolic activity : increased fluorescein uptake , such as that induced by MPS P - PQ1 - 1107 or P - 1107 , is associated with healthy , metabolically active cells . It is also unlikely that PQ - 1 alone is responsible for the minimal fluorescence intensities exhibited with PQ1 - Alex - 904 and PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 . With PQ - 1 concentration 0 . 0003 % w / v , the concentration of PQ - 1 found in MPS PQ1 - Alex - 904 , no fluorescein uptake was observed above the media or carrier control treatments . This is in line with the minimal fluorescence observed clinically with MPS PQ1 - Alex - 904 . However , with a further increase in PQ - 1 concentration to 0 . 001 % , found in MPS formulation PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 also typically associated with minimal hyperfluorescence , the median fluorescence intensity was greater than the carrier control . However a loss of metabolic activity in 0 . 001 % PQ - 1 treated L929 cells , comparable to necrosis inducer BKC , was measured 190 ( Figure 42 ) . These findings are in contrast to our previous work that fluorescein uptake is unrelated to necrosis . This suggests that concentrated solutions of PQ - 1 may utilise unconventional fluorescein uptake mechanisms compared to other MPS components or formulations , similar to the alternative PATH hypothesis . Further investigation into the hyperfluorescence inducing properties of PQ - 1 is required to fully understand its underlying mechanism . Note the metabolic activity of cells measured seen in Figure 42 is not directly comparable to those cells used to quantify fluorescein fluorescence intensities ( seen in Figure 44 ) . To this end , assuming that this concentration of PQ - 1 consistently causes a similar loss of metabolic activity seen in Figure 42 , these findings suggest that high concentrations of PQ - 1 may have greater fluorescein uptake capabilities despite the loss of metabolic activity than all other concentration of PQ - 1 , and indeed PHMB . This is perhaps due to the different interaction mechanisms employed , where PQ - 1 has been shown to intercalate into the biomembrane structure whereas PHMB adsorbs onto the surface ( Horner et al . 2015 ) . The relative extent of cytotoxicity of these biocides against mammalian cells appears uncertain . The cytotoxicity of PHMB - based MPS ReNu® Multi - purpose solution and PQ - 1 based MPS Opti - Free® Express ( amongst other solutions ) on rabbit corneas was evaluated using scanning electron microscopy . Compared to the saline control and compared to all other MPS tested , the ReNu® Multi - purpose solution induced significant physiological changes to the corneal epithelium ( Begley et al . 1994b ) . In contrast , a number of in vitro studies however also report increased toxicity with PQ - 1 based solutions ( McCanna et al . 2008 ; Mowrey - McKee et al . 2002 ; Tchao et al . 2002 ) emphasising the discrepancies in in vitro and in vivo toxicity studies . The effects of biocidal activity of these biocides are nevertheless much clearer . The biocidal activity of PHMB - based MPS are greater than PQ - 1 : a very recent biocidal efficacy study was 191 performed on Gram - negative organisms associated with corneal infiltrative using PHMB - and PQ - 1 - containing MPS . Overall , MPS containing PHMB ( and those containing Alexidine , an alternative biocide found in some MPS formulations ) demonstrated greater biocidal activity than PQ - 1 and MAPD ( myristamidopropyl dimetthylamine ) - based solutions ( Callahan et al . 2017 ) . This is in line with the findings of Groemminger and colleagues whom also report PHMB - based solutions demonstrate greater activity against Staphlacoccus aureus and Fusarium solani than PQ - 1 based solutions ( Groemminger et al . 2007 ) . Metabolic activity measurement could not be performed for cells also being analysed for fluorescein uptake , and this is a limitation of this study . This is due to the design of the fluorescein uptake assay : fluorescein treated cells are repeatedly washed with cold PBS before analysis to reduce fluorescein efflux ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) , and performing a metabolic activity assay after this would not be an accurate representation of cell viability . Live / dead using Hoechst 33342 and PI staining could not be performed using HCA as a bleed - through in the green ( fluorescein ) and red ( PI ) channels had been observed . Furthermore , varying effects on fluorescein uptake were observed with borate buffer treatment , at times exhibiting fluorescence less than the media control as seen in Figure 44 , and other times exhibiting fluorescence more than the media control , seen in Figure 45 . Loss of fluorescein is typically a consequence of the washing step , therefore future work would include optimising this step to reduce the variability in fluorescence intensities measured for borate buffer / fluorescein treated cells . 192 6 . 6 . Conclusions In conclusion , mitochondrial oxidative phosphorylation is not required for increased fluorescein uptake , and increased hyperfluorescence is unlikely to be a receptor - mediated or macropinocytic process . PHMB and PQ - 1 at low concentrations can cause limited increased hyperfluorescence , though not to the levels apparent after treatment with the hyperfluorescence - inducing MPS formulations P - PQ1 - 1107 or P - 1107 . 193 Chapter 7 Conclusions , Limitations and Future work 194 7 . 1 . Overall conclusions It has long been in practice that fluorescein hyperfluorescence is indicative of poor ocular health . Fluorescein fluorescence intensity itself however is widely known to be affected by concentration ( Romanchuk 1982 ) , although the literature surrounding other variables such as pH and temperature and fluorescein intensity is conflicting and inconsistent . There is also currently little information regarding how fluorescein intensity may affect clinical observations on the ocular surface . Solution induced corneal staining occurs with exposure to certain contact lens / MPS combinations , where increased fluorescence is typically described as a result of MPS toxicity . It is however unclear whether ' MPS toxicity ' is directly related to an increase in fluorescein uptake . The mechanisms underpinning this phenomenon are also unclear . One mechanism increasingly explored is that fluorescein fluoresces from within the cell body , in contrast to the current theories of surface pooling and the ingress model ( Morgan & Maldonado - Codina 2009 ) . A radically alternative theory , known as the PATH ( preservative associated transient hyperfluorescence ) hypothesis , proposes that an increase in hyperfluorescence is mediated by the biocide component of the MPS formulation ( Bright et al . 2012 ) . The hyperfluorescence inducing abilities of individual components however have not been thoroughly investigated . Therefore , the aims of this research were to ( 1 ) to develop a method to quantify fluorescein hyperfluorescence in cell culture , ( 2 ) investigate variables that may affect the fluorescence of fluorescein at time of observation , and determine the concentration of fluorescein available at the ocular surface ( 3 ) identify biological mechanism ( s ) underpinning fluorescein uptake in cell culture and ( 4 ) investigate MPS components for their respective hyperfluorescence inducing abilities . 195 Developing a method to quantify fluorescein hyperfluorescence in cell culture 7 . 1 . 1 . Using high content analysis ( HCA ) the fluorescein uptake in a cell population was quantified per cell as described in Chapter 3 . This method developed to quantify the fluorescein fluorescence builds on the previous work by Bakkar where hyperfluorescence is expressed as a percentage of the total population ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) . Before the study in 2014 by Bakkar and colleagues ( Bakkar et al . 2014 ) , HCA by ArrayScan had not been used for the purpose of fluorescein hyperfluorescence quantification , and fluorescein hyperfluorescence was typically investigated using fluorescence microscopy and pixel intensity quantification . When the latter method was explored as a possible methodology for fluorescein quantification in this thesis , it was found to be inaccurate and time - consuming . Fluorescein quantification by flow cytometry was also explored alongside fluorescein quantification by HCA . As it is unclear however to what extent trypsination ( required to transfer normally adherent cells to the flow cytometer ) affects cellular ability to hyper - fluoresce , an advantage of using HCA to quantify hyperfluorescence is that cells remain attached to the tissue plastic . HCA allows for collection of large quantities of data with minimal subsequent processing of the data collected similar to flow cytometry , reducing human error and increasing throughput . Investigating variables that may affect the fluorescence of fluorescein on the 7 . 1 . 2 . ocular surface As seen in Chapter 4 , variables such as pH and temperature are unlikely to affect the intensity of fluorescence observed on the ocular surface . Notably , MPS formulations of varying surfactant and biocide composition do not affect fluorescein fluorescence intensity , and is comparable to the fluorescence intensity of fluorescein prepared in PBS . Consistent with the literature , fluorescein concentration was identified as the main variable that affects the intensity of fluorescein ( Romanchuk 1982 ) , where concentrations above 0 . 05 % w / v 196 fluorescein in this work exhibited quenching of fluorescence intensity . To investigate the concentration of fluorescein available at the ocular surface at time of observation , a novel method to elucidate the concentration of fluorescein in the tear film was developed . After fluorescein application using a 1 % Minims in 2 subjects , the concentration of fluorescein rapidly decreased over a 10 minute period . Using this instillation method , these data from 2 subjects indicate fluorescence is quenched for at least 1 minute after initial fluorescein instillation . However , this work would benefit from a large clinical study before discussing these findings in a clinical setting . Identifying biological mechanism ( s ) underpinning fluorescein uptake in cell culture 7 . 1 . 3 . Those MPS associated with increased levels of clinical hyperfluorescence , P - PQ1 - 1107 and P - 1107 , also exhibited increased fluorescein uptake in both murine fibroblasts and in human corneal cells . Also demonstrated in these two cell lines was the minimal hyperfluorescence of those MPS clinically associated with low levels hyperfluorescence ( PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 and PQ1 - Alex - 904 ) . Most significantly , increased hyperfluorescence was demonstrated in viable , metabolically active cells only . Notably , the minimal hyperfluorescence exhibited with solutions PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 and PQ1 - Alex - 904 was found to be associated with the loss of cellular metabolic activity . Furthermore , contrary to a recent suggested theory ( Bandamwar et al . 2014 ) , it was also identified that hyperfluorescence is unrelated to apoptosis . With respects to the clinical application and interpretation of hyperfluorescence , this work strongly indicates that the conventional view of ‘hyperfluorescence is indicative of cell death or MPS toxicity’ requires reviewing . The reports that fluorescein uptake is an energy dependent process was also investigated , and was identified as a dynamin - associated process ( Chapter 5 ) . Dynamin is implicated in a number of endocytic pathways responsible for uptake of cargo from the cellular cytoplasm . Dynamin however is typically unrelated to macropinocytosis , an endocytic 197 pathways for bulk - fluid uptake , and was indeed not associated with MPS induced fluorescein uptake when investigated using fluorescently tagged dextran . Interestingly , an increased macropinocytic response to those MPS formulations typically associated with minimal hyperfluorescence , PQ1 - Alex - 904 and PQ1 - Aldox - 1304 , was observed . These data indicate that macropinocytosis is induced on exposure to certain MPS unrelated to increased fluorescein uptake . Not only this , the works in these studies suggest that oxidative phosphorylation is not rate limiting to fluorescein uptake , and that it is also unaffected by serum starvation indicating hyperfluorescence is likely unrelated to receptor mediated endocytosis ( Chapter 6 ) . Investigating MPS components for their respective hyperfluorescence inducing 7 . 1 . 4 . abilities MPS formulations P - PQ1 - 1107 and P - 1107 are both associated with increased hyperfluorescence , and also both comprise of non - ionic surfactant Tetronic 1107 at concentration 1 % w / v . At this concentration , Tetronic 1107 was seen to increase hyperfluorescence in both murine fibroblasts and human corneal cells with minimal effect on cell metabolic activity , seen in Chapter 5 . When PHMB and PQ - 1 were also tested ( in Chapter 6 ) , it was seen that hyperfluorescence increased at low concentrations however not to the extent of those hyperfluorescence inducing MPS P - PQ1 - 1107 or P - 1107 . These data suggest that hyperfluorescence inducing abilities of MPS formulations are most likely an effect of the surfactant component , and not the biocides as previously thought . 7 . 2 . Limitations The background fluorescein intensity often induced saturation in the images taken of the cell population and so this model required washing steps . This introduced variability , which was reduced but not eliminated by controlling the volumes of PBS used to wash the cells . The model is also highly sensitive to temperature and thus all experiments were performed on ice . In the instances of HCA fluorescein quantification , 96 well plates were 198 kept cold by using an ice press on the surface of the plate during analysis reducing the variability introduced by temperature fluctuations . Additionally due to the high - throughput nature of this method , thousands of cells could be analysed rapidly at once further minimising the variability caused by temperature . However , in the instance of fluorescence microscopy cells could not be kept cold when on the microscopy stage . This was a limitation of the microscopy equipment available . A temperature - controlled stage however would help reduce the amount of fluorescence lost over time in the future . Necrosis assays ( using PI ) , and fluorescein uptake assays could not be performed concurrently in the same cell populations due to the overlap in green ( fluorescein ) and red ( PI ) spectrums on the HCA equipment used throughout this work . That is , the cell viability of the cells from which fluorescein fluorescence intensities were recorded could not be measured . Alternatively , MTT assays in parallel to fluorescein quantification assays were regularly performed instead . However , this was also limiting as MTT assay measurements could not be performed of the same cells that were being measured fluorescein uptake . Finally , the borate buffer and the MPS components used in this work were obtained commercially . For example , the PHMB is a Cosmocil 20 % v / v solution , which may not be the same PHMB solution used in our test MPS formulation . The variation in commercially and industrially available MPS components needs further investigation . 7 . 3 . Future work This work has established an in vitro model where the effects of MPS formulations and fluorescein uptake can be studied . Using this in vitro model , investigation of further MPS formulations and MPS components in the future would allow the building of a database that could potentially be used to predict the performance of MPS on the corneal surface . This may be of interest to practitioners and industrial researchers alike . Further 199 development of the model , so as to more closely replicate clinical fluorescein uptake , would see a multi - layer cell model using cells cultured from the cornea , with a working lacrimal component . Additionally , given that not only MPS formulations but also lens materials contribute to SICS , continued development of the model in this work would incorporate lens material into these studies . The GTP - ase dynamin has been found to be associated with fluorescein uptake . However , dynamin is also known to associate with actin filaments , and both are implicated in a number of endocytic pathways . Further investigation into the precise dynamin related mechanisms , and the relationship of such mechanisms with fluorescein uptake , is an area for future work . This could be investigated using a combination of endocytic pathways inhibitors , or by using cellular knockouts of specific mechanisms . Finally , the surfactant Tetronic 1107 was found to be a hyperfluorescence - inducing component . Interactions of this compound and mammalian cells , its absorption into various contact lens materials , and additionally the mechanism behind increased fluorescein uptake induced by Tetronic 1107 is to be next investigated . Furthermore , literature and clinical studies regarding SICS could be re - analysed with these findings in mind : surfactants are likely the hyperfluorescence inducing components in MPS formulations , and not biocides such as PHMB or PQ - 1 . 7 . 4 . Summary The main outcomes of this work were ( 1 ) development of a robust quantitative method that emulates clinical hyperfluorescence in cell culture , ( 2 ) development of a unique method to elucidate the concentration of fluorescein on the ocular surface ( 3 ) correlating those MPS associated with minimal hyperfluorescence with loss of cell viability ( 4 ) identification of dynamin as a protein associated with fluorescein uptake , and ( 5 ) identification of surfactant 200 Tetronic 1107 as the hyperfluorescence inducing component , in contrast to biocides PHMB and PQ - 1 . 201 References Abreau , K . et al . , 2016 .
